Master’s Thesis (30 ECTS)
Food Allergy: Competitive Basophil Histamine Release for
Evaluating the Eﬀect of Fish Allergen Speciﬁc Immunotherapy.
Reduced 
Histamine
Release 
Students of Pharmaceutical Design & Engineering, DTU:
Diana Worm Jensen, s162893, and Veronika Naja Vilhelmsen, s123878
Internal Supervisor, DTU Bioengineering: Gregers Jungersen
External Supervisors, Laboratory of Medical Allergology, Gentofte Hospital:
Lars K. Poulsen and Bettina M. Jensen
Sunday 19th August, 2018
==PAGE:2==
==PAGE:3==
Abstract
Allergen speciﬁc immunotherapy (AIT) is a well-established treatment for allergic asthma
and rhinitis, but for food allergy, the indications for AIT are not deﬁnite. In food AIT, a
gradual increase in dosage of the oﬀending allergen purposely generate inhibitory speciﬁc-
IgG (sIgG)/sIgG4 antibodies. These sIgG/sIgG4 antibodies are considered to inhibit sIgE
binding to allergens or directly induce an inhibitory eﬀect on mast cells and basophils,
preventing activation, degranulation and histamine release (HR).
One of the major IgE-mediated food classes causing allergies is ﬁsh. Currently, no treatment
exist, besides strict avoidance and anti-allergic drugs. To establish a treatment against ﬁsh
allergy, the EU-funded FAST (Food Allergy Speciﬁc Immunotherapy) project was initiated
in 2008 to develop a vaccine composed of the major ﬁsh allergen β-parvalbumin, using the
recombinant hypoallergenic mutant carp β-parvalbumin: mCyp c 1.0101 (mCyp c 1). In
this thesis, the eﬀect of the mCyp c 1 was investigated in terms of its capacity to reduce
basophil HR through sIgG induction. As a proof of concept of the inhibitory eﬀect of
sIgG, rabbit models using rabbit sera containing sIgG against the codﬁsh β-parvalbumin:
Gad c 1 were developed and assessed by competitive Gad c 1 ELISA and by designing and
performing the biological Competitive Passive Sensitization (PS) Basophil HR immunoas-
say. These assays revealed an inhibitory eﬀect of sIgG, which lead to the development of
Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA and Competitive PS Basophil HR assays using sera from 14
codﬁsh allergic patients from the FAST phase IIa study analyzed before (Pre) and after
(Post) mCyp c 1 immunotherapy. In the Competitive PS Basophil HR immunoassay each
patient sera were used to passively sensitize basophils obtained from healthy blood donors,
to acquire a unique surface sIgE proﬁle corresponding to the patient’s serological proﬁle.
By changing the sIgE proﬁle, it was possible to quantify the HR by stimulating Pre- and
Post-sera from the FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 study with the β-parvalbumins: Gad c 1 and
recombinant Cyp c 1.
Comparing the HR from before and after immunotherapy, an HR-reduction was observed
after immunotherapy for all active-treated patients. In fact, 6 active-treated patients out
of 14 (including 3 placebos) induced a low %HRPost/Pre ratio of ≤0.64 corresponding to
a ≥36% HR-reduction. This HR-reduction correlated roughly with the induction of sIgG
and signiﬁcantly with sIgG4 measured by the biochemical ImmunoCAP® system.
These ﬁndings supported the hypothesis about the inhibitory sIgG and especially IgG4
antibodies induced by FAST mCyp c 1, verifying their ability to compete with sIgE for
β-parvalbumin binding leading to reduced HR in patients with ﬁsh allergy. Given that a
reduced HR was observed after mCyp c 1 immunotherapy identiﬁes the PS Basophil HR
immunoassay as a biological tool for evaluating the eﬀect of food AIT.
i
==PAGE:4==
Resumé
Allergen speciﬁk immunoterapi (AIT) er en veletableret behandling mod allergisk astma
og høfeber, men for fødevareallergi er eﬀekten af AIT ikke klinisk veldokumenteret. I føde-
vare AIT, gives en øget dosis af allergenet som generere inhiberende speciﬁkke IgG (sIgG)
antistoﬀer. Disse sIgG/sIgG4 antistoﬀer formodes at hæmme de speciﬁkke IgE (sIgE) anti-
stoﬀers binding til allergenet eller direkte inducere en hæmmende virkning på mastceller og
basoﬁle granulocytter, hvorved aktivering, degranulering og histaminfrigivelse forhindres.
Fisk tilhører en af de fødevaregrupper som forårsager IgE-medieret allergi. I øjeblikket ek-
sisterer der ingen behandling udover at undgå indtaget af ﬁsk og ved brug af antiallergiske
lægemidler. I 2008, blev det EU-ﬁnansieret FAST (Food Allergy Speciﬁc Immunotherapy)
projekt påbegyndt, for at udvikle en vaccine til behandlingen af ﬁske allergi. Vaccinen
indeholdte ﬁskeallergenet β-parvalbumin fra karpe (Cyp c 1), som ved recombination re-
sulterede i den muterede hypoallergeniske mCyp c 1.0101 (mCyp c 1).
I dette kandidatspeciale blev eﬀekten af mCyp c 1 undersøgt for dets evne til at inducere
sIgG og sIgG4 og derved reducere basoﬁl histaminfrigivelse. For at validere sIgGs hæm-
mende eﬀekt, blev der først udviklet kaninmodeller, hvor kanin sera indeholdende sIgG
mod torskeallergenet: Gad c 1 blev evalueret og testet i Gad c 1 ELISA samt det biologisk
udviklede immunoassay: Kompetitiv Passiv Sensitization (PS) Basoﬁl Histaminfrigivelse.
Disse analyser afslørede en hæmmende virkning af sIgG, som førte til udviklingen af: Kom-
petitiv Gad c 1 ELISA og Kompetitiv PS Basoﬁl Histaminfrigivelse immunoassays som
anvendte sera fra 14 torskeallergiske patienter fra FAST fase IIa studiet analyseret før
(Præ) og efter (Post) mCyp c 1 immunoterapi. I det Kompetitiv PS Basoﬁl Histaminfrigi-
velse immunoassay blev hvert patientsera brugt til at passive sensibilisere basoﬁle fra raske
bloddonorer, for at give en unik sIgE-proﬁl svarende til patientens serologiske proﬁl. Ved
at ændre sIgE-proﬁlen var det muligt at kvantiﬁcere histaminfrigivelsen ved at stimulere
Præ- og Post-sera fra FAST mCyp c 1 studiet med Gad c 1 og rekombinant Cyp c 1.
Ved at sammenligne mængden af histamin frigivet før og efter immunoterapien blev en
reduktion observeret efter immunoterapien for alle aktive behandlede patienter. Faktisk
inducerede 6 aktive behandlede patienter ud af 14 (inklusiv 3 placebo) en lav %histamin-
frigivelsePost/Præ med en ratio på ≤0,64 svarende til en ≥36% histaminreduktion. Denne
reduktion korrelerede i grove træk med induktionen af sIgG og signiﬁkant med sIgG4 målt
med det biokemiske ImmunoCAP® system.
Disse resultater understøttede hypotesen om at hæmmende IgG antistoﬀer, især sIgG4,
induceret fra FAST mCyp c 1 konkurrerer med sIgE for β-parvalbumin bindingen, hvilket
fører til en reduceret histaminfrigivelse hos patienter med ﬁskeallergi. I betragtning af at
en reduceret histaminfrigivelse blev konstateret efter mCyp c 1 immunoterapi identiﬁcerer
PS Basophil HR immunoassayet som et biologisk værktøj til eﬀektvurdering af fødevare
AIT.
ii

Preface
This Master’s Thesis (30 ECTS credits) represent the work for obtaining a master degree in
Pharmaceutical Design and Engineering, at the Department of Biotechnology and Biomedicine
at the Technical University of Denmark. The thesis was supervised by the internal supervisor
Gregers Jungersen, Department of Immunology & Vaccinology - Adaptive Immunology at the
Institute of Biotechnology and Biomedicine at the Technical University of Denmark.
The thesis was conducted in partnership with the Laboratory of Medical Allergology (LMA) at
Gentofte Hospital in a time frame of 5 months from March to August 2018 under the supervision
of Lars K. Poulsen and Bettina M. Jensen.
Master’s Thesis, Sunday 19th August, 2018
Diana Worm Jensen
Veronika Naja Vilhelmsen

==PAGE:13==
1. INTRODUCTION
1
Introduction
Food allergy is a major health concern aﬀecting individuals worldwide. In Europe, the Euro-
pean Academy of Allergy and Clinical Immunology (EAACI) estimated a self-reported lifetime
and point prevalence of 17% and 6%, respectively and a prevalence of <1% conﬁrmed by dou-
bled blinded placebo-controlled food challenge (DBPCFC) (Muraro and Roberts, 2014; Sicherer
and Sampson, 2017). The DBPCFC is a reliable method used as the gold standard for diag-
nosing patients with class I (IgE-mediated) hypersensitivity. Other approaches for diagnosing
an allergy, include the use of serological in vitro testing for speciﬁc-IgE (sIgE) levels, in vivo
provocation skin-prick tests (SPT), a physical examination and the patient’s symptom history
(Muraro and Roberts, 2014). The results from these tests can be used in combination to reach
a ﬁnal diagnosis.
The major contributors of IgE-mediated food allergy, involve eight allergenic food classes: ﬁsh,
shellﬁsh, cow’s milk, hen’s egg, peanuts, tree nuts, soy, and wheat (Figure 1) (FDA, 2004).
Figure 1: "The Big Eight". Referring and enforced by FDA in public law (FDA, 2004) to the eight most
common allergenic food classes: milk, egg, ﬁsh (bass, ﬂounder, or cod), shellﬁsh (crab, lobster, or shrimp),
peanuts, tree nuts (cashew, almond, pecan, walnut), soy and wheat. These eight major foods cause IgE-mediated
class I hypersensitivity reactions in more than 90 % food allergic cases (FDA, 2004). Figure Modiﬁed from Smith
(2015).
For these IgE-mediated food allergies to become manifested in susceptible individuals, a series
of steps are required; exposure to the oﬀending food allergen (even low doses), development of
allergen-speciﬁc IgE (sIgE) antibodies, sensitization upon binding of sIgE through IgE receptors
on mast cells and basophils, re-exposure to the same or a homologous allergen, crosslinking of
membrane-bound IgE receptors, cell activation and subsequently mediator release (e.g. his-
tamine release (HR); a prominent contributor in allergy), with following reactions in end-organs
(Swoboda et al., 2002, 2007).
One of the major IgE-mediated allergens found in ﬁshes is parvalbumin. Parvalbumin together
with other minor ﬁsh allergens accounts for the observed prevalence of ﬁsh allergy. Here, the
overall lifetime prevalence of self-reporting ﬁsh allergy is estimated to be 0-7 %, whereas the
prevalence range from 0.1 % to 0.7 % when SPT, sIgE levels, and food-challenge are the assessed
methods (Muraro and Roberts, 2014; Moonesinghe et al., 2016). Fish allergy is estimated to
be higher in younger age groups and in industrialized countries with high ﬁsh consumption and
processing (can attain a prevalence of 1 per 1000 individuals) (Swoboda et al., 2002; Muraro
and Roberts, 2014).
1
==PAGE:14==
1. INTRODUCTION
Typically, ﬁsh allergy remains persistent in adulthood, unlike other food allergies such as cow’s
milk allergy and hen’s egg allergy which are frequently outgrown in adulthood (Douladiris et al.,
2015).
Clinical IgE-mediated symptoms in sensitized allergic ﬁsh patients can vary from mild local
reactions to the more severe systemic reactions of anaphylaxis, representing a serious life-threat
for ﬁsh allergic patients (Swoboda et al., 2002, 2007; Zuidmeer-Jongejan et al., 2012). Even
though life-threatening symptoms exist, there is currently no preventive treatment against ﬁsh
allergy. The only treatment for ﬁsh allergy is by avoidance of ﬁsh and ﬁsh products or by treat-
ing symptoms with medicaments such as antihistamines, corticosteroids, bronchodilators, and
epinephrine. Therefore, the need for developing a safe and eﬀective treatment to ﬁsh allergic
patients is highly demanded (Zuidmeer-Jongejan et al., 2012).
In 2008 the EU-funded FAST (food allergy-speciﬁc immunotherapy) project was initiated, aim-
ing at developing a novel ﬁsh vaccine. The FAST ﬁsh project was based on a subcutaneous
immunotherapy (SCIT) and composed of the aluminum hydroxide (alum)-adsorbed recombi-
nant hypoallergenic mutant carp parvalbumin, mCyp c 1 (Zuidmeer-Jongejan et al., 2015).
From August 2013 to October 2014, the FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 phase IIa study (study information
in Appendix A, (Malling, 2013)) demonstrated the SCIT mCyp c 1 to be safe at high doses,
meaning the patients could tolerate high doses also in comparison to wildtype Cyp 1 (wtCyp c
1) formulations (Zuidmeer-Jongejan et al., 2015; Douladiris et al., 2015).
In October 2015, FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 phase IIb randomized DBPC clinical trial was initiated
and ﬁnalized in April 2017 (Stavroulakis, 2015). The phase IIb primary readout showed no
eﬀectiveness in the treatment and could not detect any solid diﬀerences in the SPT challenged
with ﬁsh in the active treatment compared to placebo. Excitingly, a notable induction of sIgG-
blocking antibodies towards native ﬁsh allergen was induced by the treatment in all patients
(unpublished results from FAST project, provided by Lars K. Poulsen). These sIgG-blocking
antibodies potentially lead to the inhibition of ﬁsh-induced mast cell and basophil HR and a
reduction in IgE/TH2 response (Swoboda et al., 2007). Therefore, more clinical sensitive stud-
ies must be designed in order to understand and evaluate the biological mechanism behind this
novel FAST mCyp 1 vaccine. For that reason, this Master’s Thesis was initiated to focus on
developing a biological immunoassay testing serum from 14 codﬁsh allergic patients before (Pre)
and after (Post) FAST ﬁsh immunotherapy. Potentially, this biological immunoassay will allow
identiﬁcation of basophil HR as a measurable indicator for validation of the eﬃcacious FAST
ﬁsh mCyp c 1.
In the following sections, the theory required to answer relevant issues in the thesis is in-
troduced. Firstly, the major allergen in ﬁsh, namely parvalbumin, is introduced together with
parvalbumin’s major sensitization route. Next, the proposed immunological mechanisms and
monitoring methods for AIT and the FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 are speciﬁed.
2
==PAGE:15==
1. INTRODUCTION
1.1
Fish Allergy
1.1.1
Parvalbumin, the Major Fish Allergen
An allergen is a small antigen that commonly triggers an immune response to provoke the pro-
duction of IgE antibodies, resulting in an allergic reaction (Murphy and Weaver, 2017). Whether
a protein is categorized as allergenic and thus as an allergen, depends among other features on
its amino acid similarity in relation to humans. Primary protein structures which have amino
acid sequence identities of ≤54 % to human homologous are often considered allergenic due to
the recognition as non-self proteins leading to an immune response, whereas identities higher
than 63 % to human homologous often are referred to as rarely allergenic due to the recognition
as self-proteins being tolerated (Jenkins et al., 2007).
One such allergen, referred to as allergenic to humans, is parvalbumin; the major allergen found
in highly bony ﬁshes. Parvalbumin is a water-soluble calcium binding muscle protein of 10-12
kDa (107-110 amino acids) which facilitates calcium translocation in muscle, promoting relax-
ation followed by contraction by sequestering intracellular calcium (Pauls et al., 1996).
Parvalbumin belongs to the superfamily called EF-hand proteins, which together with tropo-
myosins and caseins are the three main families in animal food allergens. EF-hands are charac-
terized by six α-helixes organized in three ﬂexible helix-loop-helix binding motifs (AB, CD and
EF) (Figure 2a) (Kretsinger and Nockolds, 1973). The two active motifs in EF-hands; the CD
and EF, contain a 12 residue-loop each, the so-called calcium (Ca2+ ) binding site. This Ca2+
binding site stabilize the parvalbumin conformation, especially under thermodynamics condi-
tions of matter at extremely high pressure and temperature, when highly conserved residues
whose ligands (oxygens) are directly bound to the calcium ions (Figure 2b) (Moraes et al.,
2014).
Parvalbumin can exist in multiple isoforms and can be divided into two lineages, namely α-
parvalbumin (isoelectric point (pI) > 5.0) and β-parvalbumin (pI < 4.5). The α-subtype has
been demonstrated to be non-allergenic in bony ﬁshes such as cod (Bugajska-Schretter et al.,
2000), whereas the β-subtype is typically associated with allergenic properties in ﬁshes (Pauls
et al., 1996; Jenkins et al., 2007). The allergenicity of bony ﬁshes depends on the content of
β-parvalbumin, thus the concentration of parvalbumin varies with the content of ﬁsh muscle
types, but also physical and chemical changes of food processing may alter the allergenicity of
ﬁsh parvalbumin in food products (Bernhisel-Broadbent et al., 1992; Wilwert et al., 2006).

The high degree of sequence homology between ﬁsh β-parvalbumin represents high crossre-
activity between bony ﬁsh species (Kuehn et al., 2014). Crossreactivity is a phenomenon of
an IgE antibody recognizing, binding, and inducing an immune response to similar allergenic
molecules (homologs) (Popescu, 2015). Table 1 illustrates the β-parvalbumin sequence ho-
mologies between ﬁshes, representing the most consumed ﬁsh species in Europe and compares
β-parvalbumin (β1-isoforms) sequences identities.
Some of the most studied European ﬁsh β-parvalbumin with documented crossreactivity to
other ﬁsh species is the common carp (Cyprinus carpio; Cyp c 1) and members of codﬁsh
species include Baltic cod (Gadus morhua subsp. callarias; Gad c 1) and Atlantic cod (Gadus
Morhua; Gad m 1) (Table 1, blue marks). The Baltic cod is mainly found and consumed
in Scandinavia (Bagge et al., 1994), whereas the Atlantic cod is the most commonly consumed
cod in Europe. The common carp, by contrast, is a widespread freshwater ﬁsh found in lakes
and large rivers in Europe.

1. INTRODUCTION
Sometimes, the β-isoforms of Gad c 1 and Gad m 1 are confused with one another since the
alternative name for Gad c 1 is "allergen M". Surprisingly, Gad c 1 and Gad m 1 only have
68 % sequence similarity (Table 1). β-parvalbumin from carp (Cyp c 1) has demonstrated to
be crossreactive to cod β-parvalbumin having 69-81 % amino acid sequence identity (Table 1).
β-parvalbumin is mainly expressed in white fast ﬁsh muscles, but can also present in muscles of
amphibian (e.g. edible frog, Rana esculenta), mammalian (human) and avian (chicken) muscles
(Table 1) (Hilger et al., 2004; Jenkins et al., 2007).

The high crossreactivity among β-parvalbumins correlates with allergic reactions observed in
allergic individuals consuming diﬀerent ﬁsh species (Aalberse, 2000). In fact, 70-95 % of all
ﬁsh-allergic patients who mount IgE antibodies against one speciﬁc β-parvalbumin are cross-
reacting towards other homologous β-parvalbumins from other ﬁsh species, thereby classifying
β-parvalbumin as a major allergen in ﬁsh (Swoboda et al., 2002; Kuehn et al., 2014).
1.1.1.1
β-Parvalbumins used in the Present Study
In this thesis, the main focus was on β1-parvalbumin from cod (Gad c 1) and carp (rCyp c
1 and mCyp c 1), which sequences are illustrated in Figure 3. This was based on the fact
that these β-parvalbumins are involved in the FAST study and the mCyp c 1-based vaccine
was formulated to Danish ﬁsh allergic individuals. Even though codﬁsh allergy is more common
in Scandinavia than carp allergy, the vaccine is thought to be eﬀective against cod and other
highly bony ﬁshes as well, due to the shared allergenicity.

==PAGE:18==
1. INTRODUCTION
Figure 3: Alignment of β1-Fish Parvalbumins. rCyp c 1 is aligned with mCyp c 1, Gad c 1 and Gad m 1.
mCyp c 1 is modiﬁed at positions (highlighted in red): D52A, D54A, D91A, and D93A. The Ca2+ coordinating
residues are highlighted in red frame boxes. The blue, green and purple markings, indicate the identiﬁed and
proposed IgE-binding epitopes in rCyp c 1 (Untersmayr et al., 2006), Gad c 1 (Elsayed and Apold, 1983) and

Since the 1980s, the Ca2+ binding sites of β-parvalbumin have been crucial for the investi-
gation of the high crossreactivity and allergenic properties. (Elsayed and Apold, 1983). Most
ﬁsh β1-parvalbumin sequences display approximately 67-100 % sequence similarities in the Ca2+
binding sites (visualized in Appendix B) and are 100 % conserved in aspartic acid (D) residues
at position 1 and 3 (Figure 3) directly related to the binding of calcium ions. Furthermore,
the Ca2+ binding site has been associated as the major IgE-binding site, where IgE antibodies
are directed against speciﬁc B-cell epitopes on the native β-parvalbumin conformation, leading
to IgE-mediated ﬁsh allergic response (Elsayed and Apold, 1983; Moraes et al., 2014; Kobayashi
et al., 2016).
Gad c 1 and Cyp c 1 share similar IgE-binding regions, especially in the last calcium-binding
loop (Figure 3), thereby strengthening the relevance of this area as a dominant site of IgE-
binding epitopes. While Gad c 1 and Cyp c 1 share similar epitope binding sites, the Gad m
1 has only one IgE-binding region found in the last calcium-binding loop of EF-domain, which
do not overlap much of the Cyp c 1 and Gad c 1 epitopes (Figure 3). This could indicate that
Gad m 1 could have species-speciﬁc IgE-binding epitope(s) (Perez-Gordo et al., 2013).
Cyp c 1 has until now revealed and demonstrated multiple β-parvalbumin β-isoforms by the
presence of four distinct, highly homologous (> 83 %) carp isovariants (Swoboda et al., 2002).
The Cyp c 1.0101 has been the most studied isoform of the common carp and has been the ﬁrst
ﬁsh β-parvalbumin to be recombinantly expressed and puriﬁed to homogeneity.
6
==PAGE:19==
1. INTRODUCTION
In 2002 in Austria (common consumers of carp), Swoboda et al. isolated the total RNA from
carp muscle tissue and the Cyp c 1.0101 (now referred to as Cyp c 1) was then identiﬁed, PCR
ampliﬁed and cloned into vector and expressed in Escherichia coli to produce recombinant Cyp
c 1 (rCyp c 1). Since 2002, rCyp c 1 has been used for several diagnostic purposes since it
contains most of the ﬁsh IgE conformational epitopes from various ﬁsh species (Swoboda et al.,
2002).
In 2007, Swoboda et al. develop the mutated version, mCyp c 1, (Figure 3) of calcium-free
(apoform) hypoallergenic rCyp c 1 (Swoboda et al., 2007). This mCyp c 1 was explored in
this thesis, to study the biologic eﬀect of the FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1-based vaccine. This im-
munotherapy towards ﬁsh allergy using a calcium-free hypoallergen was based on the ﬁndings
that carp β-parvalbumin contains calcium-dependent conformational IgE epitopes (Bugajska-
Schretter et al., 2000). By site-directed mutagenesis, the ﬁrst and third aspartic acid (aspartate,
D) was replaced by non-polar alanine (A) residues in the calcium-binding loops of CD and EF
domain to produce the double mutant and hypoallergenic mCyp c 1 (Swoboda et al., 2007). By
changing the calcium binding capacity, by amino acid modiﬁcations in mCyp c 1, an altered
secondary structure was obtained, resulting in Ca2+ depletion, soluble β-parvalbumin chains,
no HR from basophils (up to a concentration of 1 g/ml mCyp c 1) and no skin reactions after
SPT even at high concentration (32 µg/mL of mCyp c 1) (Swoboda et al., 2007; Douladiris
et al., 2015).
Independently of the bony ﬁsh species, the major eﬀect of mCyp c 1 immunotherapy is to reduce
IgE-binding reactivity and induce IgG-blocking antibodies speciﬁc for native β-parvalbumin in
ﬁsh allergic patients, reducing the allergic response (Swoboda et al., 2007; Douladiris et al.,
2015).
1.1.2
Immunological Mechanisms of Fish Allergy
The major sensitization route for the IgE-mediated food allergen; β-parvalbumin, is via the GI
tract. Upon digestion of highly bony ﬁshes such as cod or carp (Figure 4, A), dietary proteins
become degraded into peptides and amino acids by gastric acid and digestive enzymes through-
out the GI tract, resulting in reduced protein immunogenicity due to denaturation (Valenta
et al., 2015). Even though some β-parvalbumin becomes denatured after bypassing hypoacidic
gastric conditions (e.g. pepsin digestion), degraded β-parvalbumin retains its allergenicity due
to preserved epitopes. This enables β-parvalbumin to induce an allergic response similar to
undigested β-parvalbumin at a low concentration (Untersmayr et al., 2007; Moraes et al., 2014)
and enables it to reach the small intestine, where it becomes recognized in the gut lumen as
non-self proteins by secretory IgA (Figure 4, B) (Elsayed and Aas, 1971).
Some β-parvalbumins escape this recognition and are taken up by the intestinal epithelial cells
by the extending dendrites of dendritic cells (DCs) through the intestinal epithelial or through
microfold (M) cells to lamina propria (Figure 4, B).
7
==PAGE:20==
1. INTRODUCTION
This entry might be the result of a disrupted or dysfunctional epithelial barrier by inﬂam-
mation or genetic malfunctions; a breakdown of oral tolerance (Sampson et al., 2018). DCs are
recruited to the lamina propria due to an activated gut epithelium and migrate in complex with
β-parvalbumin to Peyer’s patches (PPs) due to secretion of IL-13 and IL-4 from innate lymphoid
cell type 2 (ILC2) and basophils, respectively (Valenta et al., 2015; Shamji and Durham, 2017).
In the T-cell zone of PP, primary sensitization starts by presentation of β-parvalbumin through
major histocompatibility complex (MHC) class II expressed on DC to T-cell receptors (TCR)
on naïve CD4 T-cell (Figure 4, C1), together with co-stimulatory ligands: B7.1 (CD80) and
B7.2 (CD86) expressed by DC-binding to the co-stimulatory ligand (CD28) on naïve CD4 T-cell
(Murphy and Weaver, 2017; Sampson et al., 2018). From the subset of naïve CD4 T-cells, a dif-
ferentiation into T-helper type 2 (TH2) cells and T-follicular helper (TfH) cells is initiated. The
allergic phenotype is initiated by the secretion of interleukin IL-4, IL-5, and IL-13 by multiple
immune cells such as basophils and mast cells. The allergen presentation and cytokine secretion
result in TH2 diﬀerentiation, amplifying the TH2 cytokines (Vickery et al., 2012; Murphy and
Weaver, 2017). Simultaneously, the TfH cells undergo linked recognition in the border of the
T-cell zone and the B-cell follicle zone with β-parvalbumin primed B-cells. This occurs due to
the production of IL-21 and IL-4 by the TH2 cell and the interaction with CD40L and CD40 on
B-cells, resulting in class switching from IgM/IgG to IgE-secreting plasma cells; the hallmark
of allergic sensitization (Figure 4, C2).
The IgE-speciﬁc plasma cells leave the PP via draining lymphatics via the mesenteric lymph
node to enter the thoracic duct, which empties into the blood. Through the blood, the plasma
cells circulate back to gut lumen, producing β-parvalbumin sIgE. The sIgE becomes bound by
high-aﬃnity IgE receptors (FcϵRI) on basophils and resident submucosal mast cells, and the
individual is now said to be sensitized (Murphy and Weaver, 2017).
On a subsequent encounter, β-parvalbumin-sIgE, facilitated by β-parvalbumin recognition on
basophils and mast cells, ampliﬁes the TH2 response (Stone et al., 2010; Murphy and Weaver,
2017). When a high amount of β-parvalbumin-sIgE-FcϵRI bound complexes are crosslinking on
mast cells and basophils, a signal is transduced through the receptors, resulting in cell activation
(Figure 4, C3)(Steiner et al., 2016; Murphy and Weaver, 2017).
Mast cell activation induces an early phase reaction, the immediate hypersensitive reaction,
consisting of a classically ’wheal and ﬂare’ reaction in the skin or the mucosa (minutes after
exposure). In the early phase, granules containing intracellular mediators fuse with the cell
membrane of mast cells leading to degranulation and release of the mediators including his-
tamine and secrete cytokines (e.g. IL-4, IL-5, and IL-13), especially of the TH2 type. These
cytokines support expansion of IL-4, IL-5, and IL-13 producing ILC2, stimulates DCs, reduces
allergen-speciﬁc T-regulatory (Tregs) cells, activates more mast cells and recruits basophils,
leading to clinical manifestations such as hives (urticaria), swelling (angioedema), atopic der-
matitis (few cases), peristalsis (resulting in diarrhea and cramping), and eventual anaphylactic
shock (Figure 4, C3)(Steiner et al., 2016; Murphy and Weaver, 2017; Sampson et al., 2018).

==PAGE:22==
1. INTRODUCTION
1.2
Allergen Immunotherapy
In this section, allergen immunotherapy (AIT) and the proposed mechanism of mCyp c 1 vac-
cination in regards to FAST ﬁsh study are described as well as a more detailed description
of the induced IgG(IgG4)/IgE ratio. Furthermore, serological monitoring of AIT eﬃcacy is de-
scribed together with the introduction to basophils, which are used in this project for measuring
basophil HR.
1.2.1
The Proposed Mechanisms of AIT
Having ﬁsh allergy, strict avoidance of ﬁsh products is the main prescription to avoid allergic re-
actions. Since avoidance requires careful food selection and anti-allergy medications as security,
a signiﬁcant amount of research directed towards preventing strategies for allergic reactions are
investigated, focusing on AIT (Zuidmeer-Jongejan et al., 2012; Burks et al., 2018).
Only a few well-performed food immunotherapy studies have been conducted over the years.
These food AIT studies have mainly been focusing on the most common allergens present in egg,
milk, hazelnut and peanut, which have been explored in randomized DBPC trials with varieties
of diﬀerent food AIT forms; oral immunotherapy (OIT), sublingual immunotherapy (SLIT),
epicutaneous immunotherapy (EPIT), and SCIT (Calderón et al., 2011; Muraro and Roberts,
2014; Berings et al., 2017; Burks et al., 2018). Few studies with milk and peanut OIT-treated
patients have demonstrated signiﬁcant increases of both milk- and peanut-speciﬁc IgG4 (Skripak
et al., 2008; Jones et al., 2009). In a more recent study with EPIT-treated patients, an increase
in peanut-speciﬁc IgG4 levels and IgG4/IgE ratios have been observed, together with trends
toward reduced basophil activation and peanut-speciﬁc TH2 cytokine levels (Jones et al., 2017).
Besides these ﬁndings, there is still a lack of knowledge about IgG(IgG4)/IgE power balance,
clinical relevance of the IgG(IgG4)/IgE ratio, long-term clinical outcomes (clinical changes as
measured by symptoms and medication score) and key questions about maintenance of a non-
allergic state after AIT. Therefore, more studies on food AIT, such as the FAST mCyp c 1, are
needed to assess these knowledge gaps (Burks et al., 2018).
In the FAST ﬁsh study, SCIT is used to introduce the hypoallergenic mCyp c 1, due to its
high eﬃcacy, safety proﬁle and patient compliance (Zuidmeer-Jongejan et al., 2012). In SCIT,
subcutaneous injections with allergen extract are performed intensively with 12-16 weekly in-
jections in the build-up phase, where the dose gradually increases until a maintenance dose
(optimal dose 5-20 µg allergen), tolerated by the patient (Bousquet et al., 1998; Krishna and
Huissoon, 2011). The maintenance dose is given by injections every 4-6 week and is continued
for a period of time, to achieve sustained unresponsiveness, deﬁned as the lack of clinical reac-
tion to the oﬀending food allergen, after active AIT has been stopped for a period of time. The
duration for SCIT is often 3-5 years, however, this period is not well-deﬁned (Alvarez-Cuesta
et al., 2006) (See the detailed procedure used in the FAST phaseIIa study in Appendix A).
10
==PAGE:23==
1. INTRODUCTION
These ﬁndings in other food AIT suggest how an IgG(IgG4)/IgE immunological proﬁle in FAST
ﬁsh mCyp c 1-treated patients could be possible.
For a successful AIT; to reach sustained unresponsiveness during and after ﬁsh AIT, immune
tolerance has to be restored. This mechanism is proposed to be induced by tolerogenic reg-
ulatory DCs (DCregs) which become primed due to a gradual exposure of the hypoallergenic
mCyp c 1 administrated with alum used as an adjuvant (Zuidmeer-Jongejan et al., 2015; Burks
et al., 2018; Sampson et al., 2018), Figure 5. DCregs produces suppressor cytokines IL-27,
IL-12 and IL-10 which change the T-cell proﬁle from a TH2 to a TH1/Treg phenotype. DCregs
also induce naïve T-cells (TH0) to generate natural regulatory T-cells (nTregs) and inducible
regulatory T-cells (iTregs), which suppress TH2 cytokines and TH2 cell proliferation, leading to
a reduction in activation of mast cells and basophils (Shamji and Durham, 2017; Sampson et al.,
2018). nTregs expresses a transcription factor which mediates suppression via TGF-β and by
a direct cell to cell contact. Due to the secretion of TGF-β and IL-10 by iTregs, regulatory
B-cells (Bregs) are produced. Bregs are a subset of B-cells which have the capability to produce
IL-10, inhibiting TH2 cell proliferation and IgE production, while inducing class-switching to-
wards IgA and IgG/IgG4(Berings et al., 2017; Shamji and Durham, 2017; Sampson et al., 2018).
This production of IgG/IgG4 antibodies tailor the AIT and favor the increase of IgG(IgG4)/IgE,
indicating the abundance of IgG/IgG4 is one of the major events in the resolution of allergy
(more detailed description below in subsubsection 1.2.2), (Scott-Taylor et al., 2018).
11
==PAGE:24==
1. INTRODUCTION
Figure 5: Proposed Mechanisms of Fish AIT. (A) The initial ﬁsh allergen (β-parvalbumin) sensitization
activates epithelial cells to secrete cytokines (TSLP, IL-25, IL-33) and chemokines (CCL2, CCL20) resulting
in the recruitment of DCs. The DCs become activated and internalize the β-parvalbumin for presentation to
naïve T-cells (TH0), which induce the allergic TH2 phenotype and trigger the production of sIgE plasma cells.
Upon subsequent exposure to ﬁsh, mast cells and basophils degranulate due to crosslinking of β-parvalbumin-sIgE
bound FcϵRI complex, resulting in histamine release. (B) After retrieving FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1.01, DCregs are
stimulated to produce suppressor cytokines (IL-10, IL-12, and IL-27), which change the T-cell proﬁle from a
TH2 to a TH1 phenotype. DCregs also induce TH0 to generate Tregs (nTregs and iTregs), which suppress TH2
cytokines and TH2 cell proliferation, leading to a reduction in mast cells and basophils activation. Secretion
of IL-10 and TGF-β leads to the production of Bregs, which inhibit TH2-cell proliferation and sIgE production
while inducing an antibody class-switching towards IgG/IgG4. Bar-headed red arrows represent inhibition. Figure
modiﬁed from Shamji and Durham (2017).
1.2.2
IgG/IgG4 and IgE Responses in AIT
Based on the proposed mechanism behind AIT and the FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 described above
(subsubsection 1.2.1), a more detailed description of how IgG/IgG4 can compete against
IgE for the same binding of allergen resulting in a dampen IgE-mediated allergic response, is
described. The existence of both IgE and IgG antibody receptors on basophils and mast cells in-
dicate that both classes of antibodies are involved in the biological response to allergy (Table 2)
(Scott-Taylor et al., 2018).
The binding of IgE to FcϵRI may be among the strongest biological aﬃnities existing (Murphy
and Weaver, 2017) reﬂecting the high eﬀectiveness of cellular activation (Table 2). FcϵRI also
has an extremely slow dissociation rate (104 orders of magnitude slower than IgG receptors)
which provides high persistence of antibody engagement ensuring mast cells and basophils are
saturated with IgE/sIgE (Maenaka et al., 2001).
12
==PAGE:25==
1. INTRODUCTION
IgE is the least abundant of all Ig in blood sera and having a short half-life of IgE in serum
(Table 2) implies that a constant de novo synthesis sIgE must follow, to sustain allergen-speciﬁc
IgE levels (Manz et al., 2002). All this contribute to IgE being able to trigger the most powerful
allergic reaction and sustain allergic sensitization.

So, how come that sIgG/sIgG4 can compete against sIgE for binding to β-parvalbumin during
and after induction of FAST mCyp c 1? The reason for this can be found in the increased
serum speciﬁc-IgG (sIgG) level during AIT. Particularly sIgG4 have shown to increase in range
from 10- to 100-fold in concentration, especially during the maintenance phase (Shamji et al.,
2012; Scott-Taylor et al., 2018). Where sIgG4 have shown to be increased during AIT, the level
of sIgE have shown the opposite (Shamji and Durham, 2017). Despite discontinuation of AIT,
the inhibitory immunoreactive IgG/IgG4 antibodies that persist have either developed higher
avidity or/and higher aﬃnity and the inhibitory eﬀect have shown to persist for several years
and induce long-term eﬃcacy (James et al., 2011; Shamji and Durham, 2017).
The IgG4 antibody probably plays the most important role in the eﬃcacy of AIT, since it
reacts diﬀerently to allergens compared to other IgG subclasses (Table 2); IgG4 cannot acti-
vate the complement system, it prevent the formation of immunocomplexes of other allergen
bound IgG antibodies, it fails in immune activation (due to inhibitory FcγRIIB), it has gener-
ally lower aﬃnity to Fc-receptors, and has the lowest serum concentration of IgG (0.5 mg/mL)
(Table 2). This indicates that this subclass can have regulatory purposes instead of inﬂamma-
tory and antigen clearance functions (Cassard et al., 2012; Scott-Taylor et al., 2018).
The proposed scenarios that could explain the relations of immunomodulation by IgG/IgG4
with successful AIT and FAST mCyp c 1 and natural resolution of allergy are illustrated in
Figure 6.

(c) The Inhibitory Eﬀect.
Halves or whole IgG4 ligate to the immunoreceptor tyrosine-based inhibitory
motif (ITIM)-containing FcγRIIB without crosslinking. IgG4-FcγRIIB bound allergen complex co-engage with
activating receptors (e.g. FcϵRI, FcϵRIIA) induced by immunocomplexes (IgG1/IgG3) on basophils. When all
receptors co-engage, the inhibitory FcγRIIB exert a dominant eﬀect, induced by a negative feedback signal from
Lyn, thus inhibit the IgE responses preventing basophil activation, degranulation, and IL-4 production. IL-10
and TGF-β1 can inhibit Fyn and transcription factors required for cell survival and cytokine production.
Figure 6: The Proposed Immunomodulation by IgG/IgG4 in AIT. Created by Authors with inspiration
from (Pullen et al., 2012; Jönsson and Daëron, 2012; Scott-Taylor et al., 2018)
14
==PAGE:27==
1. INTRODUCTION
The ﬁrst proposed immunomodulation by IgG1/IgG3 immunocomplexes and IgG4 is the block-
ing eﬀect (Figure 6a). IgG4 antibodies are very unstable and about 50-70 % may be dissociated
and present in serum as monovalent halves of antibody (one heavy and one light chain) that is
separated at the inter-chain disulﬁde bond (Schuurman et al., 2001; Murphy and Weaver, 2017).
These monovalent halves or whole IgG4 together with IgG immunocomplexes can be bound to
allergens in blood, thereby reducing the amount of free allergen left for sIgE on sensitized ba-
sophils and mast cells, inhibiting degranulation (Figure 6a) (Scott-Taylor et al., 2018).
In vivo IgG4 antibodies are very ﬂexible and in approximately 33 % (Young et al., 2014) of
cases they exchange Fab-arms by swapping heavy-light chain pairs between IgG4 monovalent
molecules, to create new bispeciﬁc IgG4 antibodies with two speciﬁcities behaving as monova-
lent antibodies with less aﬃnity to each allergen (Aalberse and Schuurman, 2002; Kolfschoten
et al., 2007). Both monovalent halves and bispeciﬁc IgG4 have reduced capacity for ligation to
any Fc-receptors, crosslinking to allergens, and forming allergen immunocomplexes due to their
weak bivalent functionality (Aalberse and Schuurman, 2002; Kolfschoten et al., 2007).
The
low-aﬃnity IgG receptors; FcγR (FcγRIIA and FcγRIIIB) are potently triggered by IgG1 or
IgG3 immunocomplexes with high avidity rather than low avidity IgG4 antibodies (bispeciﬁc or
monospeciﬁc), this suggests that the allergy responses are reduced by IgG4 ligation and thus
preventing other more potently triggers from binding (Bruhns et al., 2009).
The second proposed immunomodulation is the induction of IgG4 (or IgG) production (Figure 6b).
Monovalent IgG4 bound-allergen complexes are incapable of potently crosslinking to other IgG,
thus reducing the cell activation. Instead, they can react as halves or whole IgG4 on low-aﬃnity
FcγR such as FcγRIIIA present on Tregs, monocytes, macrophages, and DCs, reducing the
allergic reaction through the production of regulatory cytokines such as IL-10 and TGF-β1 (as
illustrated in Figure 5), which especially reduce proinﬂammatory cytokines release and induces
B-cell class switching in the favor of further IgG/IgG4 synthesis (Jeannin et al., 1998; Scott-
Taylor et al., 2018).
The third proposed immunomodulation by IgG4 (Figure 6c) is binding to the inhibitory
FcγRIIB on basophils and mast cells as well as B-cells, macrophages, DCs, and neutrophils.
When the halves or whole IgG4-binding FcγRIIB complex interferes with activating FcγR bind-
ing IgG immunocomplexes (IgG1 or IgG3), negative signals triggered by the inhibitory FcγRIIB
dominates over positive signals triggered by activating FcγR. Hence, the basophils can not be
activated by these immunocomplexes and the co-engagement also control and block the basophil
activation induced by sIgE and IL-4 production, resulting in no HR (Maenaka et al., 2001; Pullen
et al., 2012; Scott-Taylor et al., 2018). In addition, the IL-10 and TGF-β1 will inhibit positive
feedback signals, thereby also contribute to inhibitory signaling, thus block basophil activation
(Scott-Taylor et al., 2018). In comparison, the mast cells have poorly expression of FcγRIIB
and may limit the inhibitory role of IgG4 (Table 2). It is not investigated in detail if these
mechanisms of inhibitory IgG/IgG4 responses (Figure 6) works biologically and mediate the
same eﬃcacy in vaccinated allergic patients and in diﬀerent forms of AIT (Cassard et al., 2012;
Scott-Taylor et al., 2018).

==PAGE:28==
1. INTRODUCTION
1.2.3
Monitoring of AIT
Since high amounts of variation regarding immunologic responses are observed during AIT, it
is diﬃcult to ﬁnd ideal predictive biomarkers that can direct the link between immunological
monitoring and clinical outcome (Shamji et al., 2017). Therefore, new quantitative measurable
biomarkers and immunological assays must be developed to identify the immunological mecha-
nism behind and the eﬀectiveness of food AIT.
Seven potential groups of biomarkers (Table 3) and their measurable compartments have been
suggested by the EAACI, to evaluate on AIT eﬃcacy. Out of the seven biomarkers, this thesis
will be focusing on the measurable compartments; serum sIgE, serum sIgG/sIgG4 and basophil
HR.
Table 3: Seven Potential Predictive Biomarkers of AIT. DAO; diamine oxidase, SPT; skin prick test.
Not all possible measurable compartments are included. Table created by Authors. Information obtained from
Shamji and Durham (2017).

Cellular biomarkers
Treg, Breg and DCreg
In vivo biomarkers
Allergen provocation tests (e.g. SPT) and chamber studies
The proposed eﬀect of food AIT and FAST mCyp c 1, as mentioned above in subsubsec-
tion 1.2.2, involves the development of a new sIgGs(IgG4)/sIgE immunological proﬁle, where
sIgG levels are increased and have developed higher avidity/aﬃnity. Even though an increase
in the serum sIgG/sIgG4 levels in food AIT have been quantiﬁed in several immunochemical
studies and IgG/IgE receptors have been studied extensively in human basophil activation test
(BAT) (e.g. assessed by CD203c and/or CD63 upregulation) by ﬂow-cytometry, there are still
questions to answer in regards to the relation of the sIgG(sIgG4)/sIgE balance related to the
biological/immunological responses in food allergic patients (Zuidmeer-Jongejan et al., 2012;
Cassard et al., 2012; Shamji et al., 2017; Shamji and Durham, 2017; Burks et al., 2018).
In regards to the immunochemical monitoring, one of the most common commercial meth-
ods for quantiﬁcation of sIgG/sIgG4 and sIgE is by the ImmunoCAP® system (Thermo Fisher
Scientiﬁc, Uppsala, Sweden). ImmunoCAP® quantiﬁcation is a highly reliable method in food
allergy and a good indicator for identiﬁcation of allergy patients and immunological responses
in relation to AIT treatment.
16
==PAGE:29==
1. INTRODUCTION
Therefore investigations of AIT eﬃcacy typically starts before receiving AIT (as the case for the
FAST study), to ﬁnd appropriate subjects for the AIT treatment: having serum sIgE antibodies
distinguishable from healthy individuals (Griﬃths et al., 2017).
The ImmunoCAP® test principle is simple and designed as a sandwich immunoassay having
the allergen of interest coated to a cellulose sponge, which ensures high binding capacity. The
serum is added and the sIgE/sIgG antibodies are bound to the allergen, independently of re-
ceptor aﬃnity. The non-sIgE/sIgG is washed away and the ﬂuid from the sponge can now be
measured by ﬂuorescence, having sIgE/sIgG antibodies amount directly proportional with the
ﬂuorescence (ThermoFisherScientiﬁc, 2018).
In the ImmunoCAP® system individuals are categorized into semi-quantitative CAP classes
according to their level of sIgE towards a certain allergen (Table 4). Belonging to CAP class 0
indicates no or limit amount of sIgE produced (expressed in kU/L (Kilo Units of IgE per Litre)
or ng/mL), 0.35 kUA/L is the typically clinical cut-oﬀ, whereas belonging to CAP class 4 (17.50
to >42.00 ng/mL) indicate a high amount of sIgE produced towards an allergen. The high sIgE
levels to an allergen correlate roughly with clinical allergy disease. However, individuals with
high sIgE levels can have no symptoms of allergy and vice versa.
Table 4: The Diﬀerent CAP® Classes. Individuals are categorized into CAP® classes depending on their
level of sIgE. The test system CAP®, is a international unit for measuring IgE. The sIgE values are expressed in
kU/L (Kilo Units of IgE per Litre), where 1 kU per IgE/L equals 2.4 ng per IgE/mL. Table created by Authors.

Before and after retrieving AIT, the sIgG/sIgG4 levels can again be measured by ImmunoCAP®.
sIgG/sIgG4 antibodies are measured in mg antigen-speciﬁc antibodies(A)/L (mgA/L) and no
cut-oﬀvalue for sIgG/sIgG4 antibodies exist unlike sIgE, as these sIgGs are not directly related
to diseases. Studies, mostly on AIT to allergic respirators diseases, have investigated how mea-
surements of increased sIgG levels in general correlates with AIT eﬃcacy and clinical outcomes.
Where a signiﬁcant increase in sIgG4 levels indicate a good chance for an immunological re-
sponse to AIT treatment, no change of levels correlates with a low chance for an eﬀective AIT
treatment (Shamji et al., 2012; Feng et al., 2018).
Opposite the immunochemical ImmunnoCAP® system, which has a high capacity to bind all
sIgE and sIgG independently of receptor aﬃnity and avidity, biological immunoassays using
human cells such as basophils, reﬂects the human biology with a higher sensitivity, requiring
high avidity and aﬃnity binding of sIgE and sIgG for basophil HR.
17
==PAGE:30==
1. INTRODUCTION
1.2.4
Human Basophils and their use in Biological Immunoassays
As described in subsubsection 1.1.2, basophils together with mast cells are key contributors
to allergy. Since blood circulating basophils are more accessible to obtain than tissue-resident
mast cells and since basophils are closer to the human mast cells than animal models and ex
vivo models (Varricchi et al., 2018), basophils are used as in vitro surrogates for mast cells in
this thesis.
Basophils are granulocytes derived from CD34+ hematopoietic stem cells in the bone marrow.
The fate of becoming fully diﬀerentiated into mature basophil is determined by two crucial
transcription factors, namely, C/EBPα and GATA2. Furthermore, IL-3 and thymic stromal
lymphopoietin (TSLP) are important key factors for priming, expansion, and survival of ba-
sophils (Figure 7) (Steiner et al., 2016; Murphy and Weaver, 2017; Varricchi et al., 2018). After
fully diﬀerentiating, the mature basophils are released into the peripheral circulation where they
account for < 1 % of the human leukocytes (Steiner et al., 2016; Shamji et al., 2017). Even
though basophils are useful tools in research, they are very fragile and have a short lifespan of
a few days (approximately 2 days), making them diﬃcult and challenging to handle (Varricchi
et al., 2018).
Basophils express a variety of receptors on their surface, including cytokine-, chemokine-,
complement-, PG-, Toll-like, and Fc- receptors (Steiner et al., 2016). The number of FcϵRI
on basophils varies substantially among individuals due to the level of serum IgE, ranging from
approx. 100.000 in non-atopic individuals to 250.000 FcϵRI in allergic hypersensitive individ-
uals (Stone et al., 2010; Varricchi et al., 2018). For induction of immediate hypersensitivity
reaction (e.g. histamine degranulation) in basophils, crosslinking of allergen-sIgE loaded high-
aﬃnity FcϵRI is needed, which requires a minimum of at least two diﬀerent IgE clones binding
to nonoverlapping allergen epitopes (Figure 7), (Christensen et al., 2010).
The diﬀerent properties of allergic IgE repertoire of individuals aﬀecting the basophils and their
release of histamine, are crucially depended on several factors, such as allergen-sIgE antibody
concentrations (the limiting factor for maximal degranulation and basophil sensitivity is the low
concentration of sIgE), overall sIgE aﬃnity for allergens and the amount of allergen epitopes
recognized by patients sIgE repertoire (clonality) (Christensen et al., 2008).
The mechanisms of basophil HR upon allergen stimulation is highly useful for evaluating AIT,
since inhibition of basophil activation, potential by allergen-sIgG blocking antibodies induced
by post-immunotherapy, is associated with the eﬀectiveness of AIT (Shamji et al., 2017). In
this thesis, by a procedure of passive sensitization (PS), reloading of sIgE antibodies to FcϵRI
obtained by the patient Pre-sera and Post-sera from the FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 treatment, makes
it possible to evaluate the change in HR level upon stimulation with ﬁsh β-parvalbumins.

the bone marrow and becomes diﬀerentiated into common myeloid progenitor, basophil progenitor and at last
mature basophil due to the regulation of transcription factors: GATA2 and C/EBPα and the priming factors:
TSLP and IL-3. The mature basophil can become activated by crosslinking of two sIgE loaded FcϵRI binding
to an allergen such as β-parvalbumin. The activation of a cascade of signaling events (mediated by kinases:
Lyn, Fyn, and Syk) induced by allergen (β-parvalbumin) result in; degranulation of mediators such as histamine,
leukotrienes, and cytokines (IL-4, IL-5 and IL-13), which stimulate diﬀerentiation of naïve T-cells (TH0) into

Summing up the introduction, the major cause of ﬁsh allergy is the most potent crossreac-
tive allergen in bony ﬁsh, namely the β-parvalbumin.
β-parvalbumin show high stability,
making allergen presentation possible to naïve T-cells and B-cells, resulting in the produc-
tion of β-parvalbumin sIgE and mediator release including histamine, due to crosslinking of
β-parvalbumin sIgE loaded FcϵRI on basophils and mast cells on subsequent exposure. There-
fore, using the mutated hypoallergenic mCyp c 1 from the FAST study seems favourable as
a potential hypoallergen, since it has high amino acid sequence similarity with natural occur-
ring β-parvalbumins (e.g.
Gad c 1 and Cyp c 1) as well as largely retain T-cell reactivity
and the capacity to induce blocking and inhibitory sIgG/sIgG4 antibodies, thus elicit reduced
IgE-reactivity and HR. The change in IgG/IgE ratio (indicate the induction of sIgG and/or re-
duction in sIgE and also change of avidity/aﬃnity) after mCyp c 1 AIT is preferably evaluated
using biological immunoassays with basophils as surrogates. Using basophils and their capacity
to release histamine upon receptor stimulation, reﬂect the human system to a higher degree
than immunochemical systems such as the ImmunoCAP® system.

==PAGE:32==
2. HYPOTHESIS AND OBJECTIVES
2
Hypothesis and Objectives
Throughout the years, the inhibitory eﬀect of IgG/IgG4 in relation to IgE-mediated allergy have
been investigated through biochemical and biological assays, to reveal the mechanism behind al-
lergy. Even though biochemical methods such as quantiﬁcation of sIgE or sIgG/sIgG4 levels are
used extensively as predictive biomarkers for evaluating AIT, the biological interplay of immune
cells is missing. In this thesis, an immunoassay reﬂecting the human biology will be developed
focusing on the interplay between IgE and IgG/IgG4 in relation to AIT towards IgE-mediated
ﬁsh allergy. This will be assessed using sera obtained from the FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 study.
From the acquired background knowledge, a hypothesis and objectives are assessed.
Hypothesis:
sIgG/sIgG4 induced by FAST mCyp c 1.0101 competes with sIgE for β-parvalbumin binding
leading to reduced histamine release in patients with ﬁsh allergy
To test the hypothesis, a biological immunoassay testing the eﬃcacy of the FAST mCyp c
1 is developed (objective 5), requiring multiple tools deﬁned in objective 1 to 4.
Objectives:
1. Produce and validate a cod ﬁsh extract containing β-parvalbumin (Gad c 1), which will
be used in ELISA and Passive Sensitization (PS) Basophil Histamine Release (HR) im-
munoassay.
2. Design and test a Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA, using rabbit sera containing sIgG against
Gad c 1 as an inhibitory tool, as a proof of concept of the inhibitory serological sIgG
eﬀect.
3. Design and test a biological Competitive PS Basophil HR immunoassay, using rabbit sera
containing sIgG against Gad c 1 as an inhibitory tool, as a proof of concept of the inhibitory
serological eﬀect in relation to sIgG/sIgE ratio and thereby β-parvalbumin competition.
4. Design and test a Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA, using human Pre-sera and Post-sera from
the FAST study, as a proof of concept of the inhibitory serological sIgG/sIgG4 eﬀect.
5. Based on objective 1 to 4, a Competitive PS Basophil HR immunoassay is developed,
using 14 human Pre-sera and Post-sera from the FAST study, to validate the inhibitory
serological eﬀect in relation to sIgG(sIgG4)/sIgE ratio and thereby β-parvalbumin com-
petition.
20
==PAGE:33==
3. METHODS
3
Methods
In this section, the methods used in this thesis for answering the 5 objectives are described.
The major methods are direct sandwich ELISA, buﬀy coat screening, and passive sensitization
(PS) Basophil HR immunoassay (Figure 8). For each method, the relevancy of the concept
is explained followed by the technical procedure. Details including the full description of the
procedure, materials and reagents can be seen in the protocols (Appendix J-L).

Figure 8: Flow Chart over the Experimental Methods. Firstly, cod extracts are produced and validated
through Gad c 1 ELISA and PS Basophil HR. Secondly, competitive immunoassays are developed using rabbit

3.1
Sera Study Population
In the human models, serum samples (stored at -20 ◦C for maintaining their quality) were col-
lected from the 14 codﬁsh allergic males or females ranging from 18-65 years, acquired from the
FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 study Pre- and Post-immunotherapy. The 14 patients were divided into
two groups based on mCyp c 1 dosage; Group 1: 5 patients (P1, P2, P3, P5, P7) received 10
single rising doses of mCyp c 1 from 0.6 ng to 6 µg and 2 maintenance doses and Group 2: 6
patients (P9, P10, P12, P13, P15, P16) received 10 single rising doses of mCyp c 1 from 6 ng to
60 µg and 2 maintenance doses. 4 patients (P4, P6, P11 and P14 (P14 not included in this the-
sis)) received placebo (Pbo). All patients had a positive case history of class 1 hypersensitivity
towards ﬁsh. sIgG, sIgG4 and sIgE levels for all patients were determined beforehand in the
FAST study (section 4) (unpublished results from FAST project, provided by Lars K. Poulsen)
and their correlations can be visualized in Appendix A and subsection A.1 together with
all other details and criteria for the FAST study.
21
==PAGE:34==
3. METHODS
In the rabbit models, the rabbit sera containing IgG (stored at -20 ◦C) were obtained from
a study in 2006 with New Zealand white rabbits SC immunized with 0.5 mg/mL Gad c 1 mixed
with an adjuvant (TiterMax). The two sera samples: named TAP 5 and TAP 6, were har-
vested from the second round of immunization; 8 and 9 months after the ﬁrst immunization
(day 0), respectively. The sIgG concentrations were measured for TAP 5 and TAP 6 by the
modiﬁed ImmunoCAP® system, yielding sIgG at 3.36 ng/mL (1.40 kUA/L) and 2.93 ng/mL
(1.22 kUA/L), respectively (Terp and Kostka, 2009).
All patient and rabbit sera samples were centrifuged initially in every experiment to avoid
possible interfering substances (the precipitate) such as lipid, bilirubin and erythrocytes left-
overs, which were visually inspected for the 14 FAST patient Pre-sera (subsection A.2). Too
many freeze-thaw cycles were avoided since this is detrimental to many serum components.
3.2
Buﬀy Coat Blood Donors
Fresh anti-coagulated buﬀy coat blood was obtained from anonymous donors at "Blodbanken
Rigshospitalet". Buﬀy coat is processed blood that contains most of the white cells (neutrophils,
eosinophils, basophils, lymphocytes, and monocytes) with a reduced number of erythrocytes and
plasma present. The blood was screened (Appendix J) and selected based on criteria explained
in subsection 3.6.
To extend the basophils lifetime and maintain their quality, diluted recombinant human IL-3 (10
pg/mL) was added to the blood suspension (day 0). Binding of IL-3 to surface receptors increases
the sensitivity of basophils leading to growth, survival and increased reactivity resulting in more
released histamine and reaction at a lower concentration to stimuli (Larsen et al., 2017). For
each conducted experiment, new blood donors were screened and managed immediately, since
basophils only have a short lifetime of a few days as described in subsubsection 1.2.4.
3.3
Allergen Material
Allergenic materials from codﬁsh and carp were used as positive controls for ﬁsh allergy and as
allergens used for PS Basophil HR challenge.
Cod extracts containing Gad c 1 were produced from diﬀerent freeze-dried cod powders related
to the FAST study: Cod 1 (from 2008, batch#1: Cod 1.1, batch# 2: Cod 1.2) and Cod 2 (from
2015). To produce the cod extract, 1 g freeze-dried cod powder was mixed with 10 mL sterile
water, centrifuged multiple times to retrieve a supernatant containing Gad c 1 (procedure de-
tails in Appendix K). Cod extracts produced from the powder typically comprise crude lipid
(≈5%) and proteins (≈80-90%) and are therefore initially centrifuged in every experiment to
avoid the pellet.
The amount of powder used was based on the threshold dose for eliciting an allergic reaction
when consuming ﬁsh, which range from 5 mg to 6 g ﬁsh meat (Taylor et al., 2002).
22
==PAGE:35==
3. METHODS
The amount was also based on literature and experiments from a previous Master’s Thesis per-
formed at LMA, stating 100 g cod ﬁsh equals approximately 0.523 g (fresh ﬁsh) and 0.144 g
(cod powder) parvalbumin (Matricardi et al., 2016; Terp and Kostka, 2009). Therefore, it was
estimated that 0.144 mg Gad c 1/mL was present in the cod extract. Since the value is an
estimation, it is used as an arbitrary unit in this thesis.
rCyp c 1 (UniProt Q8UUS3), the recombinant puriﬁed carp allergen, (described in para-
graph 1.1.1.1), was also used as a positive control for ﬁsh allergy. Since rCyp c 1 (1 mg/mL)
exists in its puriﬁed form, the reactivity was approximately 1000 fold higher than for the cod
extract and the dilution series, therefore, starts 1000 times lower.
3.4
Controls and Stimulants
Aﬃnity puriﬁed goat anti-human IgE (anti-IgE) was used as a quality measurement in
all "Buﬀy Coat Screening" and "PS Basophil HR" immunoassays, to help identify the optimal
donors and to indicate whether the biological immunoassays have been performed successfully.
Anti-IgE binds to the Fc-region of two FcϵRI, which crosslinks the receptors leading to phos-
phorylation, degranulation and release of histamine (Figure 7).
PMA/ionomycin; a solution of phorbol 12-myristate 13-acetate and ionomycin calcium salts,
were assessed in all "Buﬀy Coat Screening" and "PS Basophil HR" immunoassays performed,
to help identify optimal donors and indicate whether the biological immunoassays have been
performed successfully. PMA and ionomycin are non-IgE crosslinking substances used to ac-
tivate basophils independently of the IgE-receptors. Instead, PMA and ionomycin react with
the calcium releasing pathways, which are necessary for HR. PMA causes direct activation of
the protein kinase C, located at the end of the signaling cascade, leading to degranulation of
histamine. Ionomycin directly facilitates and enhance intracellular Ca2+ concentration causing
degranulation and releasing of histamine (Chatila et al., 1989).
The released histamine induced by anti-IgE, cod extract or rCyp c 1 stimulation were calcu-
lated as percent HR (%HR) by dividing the HR of stimuli with the maximum HR induced by
PMA/ionomycin stimulation:
%HR =
Mean HR(ng/mL)
Mean PMA/ionomycin(ng/mL)
· 100
(1)
WE pool (2012/3), containing sera from 120 healthy non-allergic patients, was used as a neg-
ative serum control and to assess whether biological immunoassays were successfully performed
based on anti-IgE and PMA/ionomycin levels. The WE pool contains non-allergic sIgE against
Gad c 1 and does therefore not mediate a ﬁsh allergic response induced by basophil HR.
23
==PAGE:36==
3. METHODS
The serological values for WE pool were measured at LMA, identifying WE pool belonging
to CAP class 0 having a concentration of <0.35 sIgE towards rGad c 1 and codﬁsh. In regards
to sIgG, the concentration reaches 2.36 mgA/L.
Normal rabbit (kanin) serum (NKS) was used as a negative serum control and as in-
hibition reference in rabbit models and used in a similar way as the WE pool. NKS is pooled
from a normal donor population of New Zealand white rabbits with normal IgG levels
In-house sera collected from 3 ﬁsh allergic patients; 1983-19, 1362-57 and 2031-23, yield-
ing sIgE levels of 57.60 ng/mL (CAP class 4), 56.88 ng/mL (CAP class 4) and 24.96 ng/mL
(CAP class 3), respectively (samples obtained and measured by the LMA). These sera were
used as an quality control to validate whether PS Basophil HR was successfully accomplished
before performing PS with the precious human FAST sera (only 1 mL available). As a proof of
concept for PS Basophil HR, patient 1362-57 (high stability through experiments) was used in
most PS performed as a reference, to be comparable with the obtained measurements.
3.5
Gad c 1 ELISA
In this thesis, a direct sandwich Enzyme-Linked ImmunoSorbent Assay (ELISA) was performed
to detect the ﬁsh allergen of interest; Gad c 1 and rCyp c 1 and to validate the codﬁsh extracts
produced. For the ELISA, polyclonal IgG antibodies are directed towards the allergens present
in codﬁsh extracts (produced from cod powders subsection 3.3) and rCyp c 1.
For coating, primary polyclonal antibodies (TAP 4: Rabbit anti-Gad c 1, 2000 ng/mL) were
used capable of binding the allergen via epitopes on antigen binding region (Fab). After adding
a 3-fold dilution series of rCyp c 1 and Gad c 1, detection biotinylated polyclonal antibodies
(Rabbit anti-Gad c 1-biotin) were added capturing the allergen at another epitope position,
resulting in a sandwich. The allergens captured were detected by adding the avidin-peroxidase
and the peroxidase substrate; o-phenyl enediamine dihydrochloride (OPD) mixed with peroxide
buﬀer, which allows the enzyme to transfer a hydrogen molecule to OPD resulting in a color
reaction.
After 15-20 min. in dark, the colorimetric reaction was stopped by acidic pH (sulphuric acid),
which change the pH so drastically so the enzyme present in the solution does not act on its
substrate, thereby terminating the reaction. The color intensity was then determined by spec-
trophotometry (ELISA reader). The optical density (OD) was measured by the ELISA reader
at 490 nm (reference 630 nm), which quantiﬁed the allergen, where the absorbance was pro-
portional to the concentration of the bound allergen. The procedure used in this thesis can be
visualized in Figure 9 and in Appendix K.
By performing the ELISA, the cod powder extract with the highest content of Gad c 1 was
identiﬁed and used in the rest of the experiments.

3.6
Buﬀy Coat Screening
Before PS Basophil HR could be successfully achieved, an optimal blood donor had to be found
to verify its feasibility in PS. The optimal donor was found by buﬀy coat screening on day zero
(day of blood receiving) using the "Direct Basophil HR" test exploiting the histamine releasing
ability of basophil activation retaining autologous IgE. An optimal donor was characterized by
having; (1) highly responsive high-aﬃnity IgE receptors (FcϵRI), (2) a high number of basophils
indicated by the high "max" HR, and (3) being non-allergic toward ﬁsh (cod and carp).
The criteria for ﬁnding the optimal buﬀy coat donor was investigated by the stimulants :
1. Anti-IgE: To investigate and to ensure the high amount of IgE-receptors expressed on ba-
sophils and to quantify whether the basophils could be activated through IgE-stimulation.
The criteria for a useful donor stimulated with anti-IgE was:
• an HR >100 ng/mL (>70-100 %HR) in the two highest dilution points. Categorized
as a "super donor".
• an HR ≥30 ng/mL (approx. 50-70 %HR) in the two highest dilution points. Cate-
gorized as an "optimal donor".
25
==PAGE:38==
3. METHODS
• an HR <30 ng/mL in the two strongest dilution points and/or <50 %HR exclude
the basophil donor. Having almost 0 %HR the donor’s basophils were categorized
as "non-releasers"; non-responsive IgE-mediated HR (Kleine Budde et al., 2001).
Approximately 5-10 % of the population show no response to IgE-crosslinking (Shamji
et al., 2017).
2. PMA/ionomycin: To investigate and ensure a high amount of basophils in the buﬀy coat
and to quantify max HR. The criteria for a useful donor stimulated with PMA/ionomycin
was:
• an HR >200 ng/mL categorized as a "super donor".
• an HR >100 ng/mL categorized as an "optimal donor".
3. Cod extract and rCyp c 1. To avoid blood donors having allergen-sIgE towards ﬁsh,
the allergenicity of the samples was tested by adding cod extract and rCyp c 1. It was
preferable to avoid donors with a ﬁsh allergy since it would bias the results. The criterion
for an optimal donor stimulated with ﬁsh allergens was:
• an HR ≤10 ng/mL. This value is used as the cut-oﬀfor ﬁsh allergy; having a value
below 10 ng/mL indicated no allergy.
The ﬁrst step when ﬁnding the optimal donor was the receiving of fresh buﬀy coats (day 0)
(Figure 10, (1)), often three diﬀerent buﬀy coats from anonymous healthy individuals. The
buﬀy coat blood was then washed and isolated by centrifugation (Figure 10, (2)) and the
plasma volume reconstituted with 1,4-piperazinediethansulfonic acid (pipes) buﬀer. Afterward,
the appropriate stimulants; anti-IgE, PMA/ionomycin, and the β-parvalbumins: cod extract
and rCyp c 1, which were diluted with pipes buﬀer, were added to the histamine (HI)-plate in
duplicates in a 3-fold dilution series. Cod extract and rCyp c 1 were added in diﬀerent con-
centrations to obtain the desired dose-response curve (Figure 10, (3)). See plate setup and
procedure in Appendix J.
Afterward, buﬀy coat was added to the HI-plate and incubated at 37 ◦C to allow histamine
binding to the glass microﬁber present in the wells. After incubation, interfering blood con-
stituents were removed by washing the plate repeatedly (with both demineralised (dm.) water
and sodium dodecyl sulfate (SDS) solution for protein denaturing and removal of unspeciﬁc
binding to glass microﬁbers), leaving histamine, released by activated basophils, bound to the
solid glass microﬁber phase.
To quantify Direct Basophil HR, a sensitive ﬂuorescent coupling reagent called ortho-phthaldi-
aldehyde (OPA) with emission at the ultraviolet light was added. OPA forms a ﬂuorescent
conjugation product when interacting with the primary amines (NH2) in histamine.
The conjugation reaction was stopped by adding perchloric acid, which lowers the pH, interrupt
the binding of OPA to the amines in histamine and makes the ﬂuorescent conjugation product
stable.
26
==PAGE:39==
3. METHODS
The HR were then quantiﬁed ﬂuorometrically, using the HistaReader (Figure 10, (4)) which
detect the light scattered on OPA coupled to histamine. The OPA-histamine molecules excite
through the ﬂow cell at 305-395 nm and emit at 430-470 nm, which are then converted into
a digital signal, visualized as OD-values. Here, the ﬂuorescence is directly proportional to the
histamine bound to the glass microﬁbers. The HistaReader has a sensitivity of 10 ng/mL and
a detection range from 0-150 ng/mL histamine. In Excel the raw data from the HistaReader
were recalculated to obtain the HR in ng/mL by using the following equation:
HR = (FX −F0)
(F50 −F0) · 50 ng
mL
(2)
FX denotes the ﬂuorescence quantiﬁed in the wells containing the samples.
F0 denotes the
mean of ﬂuorescence measured in the blank standard and F50 denotes the mean of ﬂuorescence
measured in the standard lane containing pre-coated 50 ng/mL histamine. The HR results were
then calculated to %HR (Equation 1) to equally compare the results obtained.

blood donor is received (day 0). (2) Buﬀy coat containing basophils is isolated.(3) Cell suspension (buﬀy coat
blood) with serum and selected stimulants (anti-IgE, PMA/ionomycin, cod extract and rCyp c 1) are added to
an HI-plate. The HI-plate is incubated, washed with SDS and dm. water, the chromogen; OPA is added and
the released histamine from the activated basophils are quantiﬁed by the HistaReader (4). From the quantiﬁed
HR, the maximal %HR of basophils is measured using PMA/ionomycin, the responsiveness of FcϵRI receptors is
tested using anti-IgE and whether the donor is allergic to ﬁsh is tested using cod extract and rCyp c 1. Created

3. METHODS
3.7
PS Basophil HR
After ﬁnding the optimal buﬀy coat donor on day 0, PS with In-house sera (1362-57) was per-
formed as a quality control of the buﬀy coat on day 0 or 1. On day 1 or 2, PS with serum (either
from rabbit sera or human FAST sera) was performed followed by quantiﬁcation of basophil HR
in an immunoassay with same quantiﬁcation procedure as described in (subsection 3.6). See
procedure of PS Basophil HR in Appendix L.
Opposite Direct Basophil HR, exploiting a healthy donor’s autologous antibodies (mainly IgE)
for its histamine releasing abilities, PS (also called "Indirect" Basophil HR) makes it possible
to investigate the HR with an allergic proﬁle. By stripping oﬀthe donors autologous IgE, the
basophils can be PS to a proﬁle of a ﬁsh allergic patient which then can be challenged with
allergens.
In PS Basophil HR, isolated basophils obtained from the optimal buﬀy coat blood donor (sub-
section 3.6) was centrifuged with an alkali salt solution to stabilize the basophils and their
osmolality. The supernatant was then removed without disturbing the white cell layer and re-
constituted and centrifuged with cold acidic ’stripping’ buﬀer to dissociate the autologous IgE
antibodies (also other surface antibodies) from the basophils surface receptors. This allowed PS
where heterologous sIgE sera (sera from allergic patients largely with sIgE) could be added to
each cell suspension (buﬀy coat blood) to saturate and reload sIgE to FcϵRI binding sites on
basophils creating an allergenic proﬁle (Figure 11).
Optimal  basophil  
with  autologous  IgE  
Stripping  of  
IgE  by  acidic  
buffer
(<4  pH)  
Passive  
sensitization  
Optimal  basophil  with  
heterologous  allergen  
sIgE  
Stripped  basophil
Figure 11: The Process of Passive Sensitization. Firstly, autologous IgE antibodies are stripped from
the donor basophil surface by applying a buﬀer with low pH (≤pH 4). After stripping, the basophil is incubated
with serum sIgE proﬁle, which saturates the basophil by reloading its sIgE to FcϵRI. The basophils can now be
challenged with stimulants and allergens (β-parvalbumin), illustrated in Figure 10 step 3 and 4), now allergen
also leads to histamine release due to the ﬁsh allergenic proﬁle. Created by Authors.
After centrifugation with stripping buﬀer, the supernatant was removed and reconstituted with
pipes buﬀer to restore pH followed by another round of centrifugation. Again the supernatant
was removed and the cell suspension (containing the stripped basophils) were mixed and ready
for PS with sera by 1 h. of incubation.
28
==PAGE:41==
3. METHODS
For the PS Basophil HR to be successful, appropriate stimulants and controls were included
to stimulate basophil HR (subsection 3.4); allergens containing β-parvalbumin (cod extract,
rCyp c 1), anti-IgE and PMA/ionomycin as positive controls, and WE pool serum as the nega-
tive control for ﬁsh allergy. Again, the quantiﬁcation of basophil HR was performed as described
in (subsection 3.6) and illustrated in Figure 10 step 3 and 4.
As for the buﬀy coat screening, criteria for an optimal PS Basophil HR immunoassay was
determined, by having a:
1. Cut-oﬀlevel. Only HR or %HR values above the cut-oﬀlevel of 10 ng/mL or 10 %HR.
Values beneath are not detected by the HistaReader with accuracy. The cut-oﬀlevel was
determined by the calibration plate which measures down to 10 ng/mL.
2. Quality control. To ensure PS has been performed successfully, the HR range for anti-
IgE, cod extract and rCyp c 1 were identiﬁed for WE pool and 1362-57. 1362-57; the
HR peak range for anti-IgE: 60-80 HR%, cod extract: 35-60 %HR and rCyp c 1: 40-60
%HR. WE pool; the HR for cod extract and rCyp c 1 should be <10 %HR. WE pool
was included as well in every PS setup to avoid measuring of free histamine not related
to IgE-mediated responses. All the values above are founded on experiments performed
with 1362-57 and WE pool
3. Suﬃcient anti-IgE response. The anti-IgE HR should be over the HR cut-oﬀof 17
ng/mL, which indicate successful PS. The cut-oﬀvalue was based on an experiment per-
formed with non-PS (NPS), where cell suspension was mixed with pipes buﬀer instead of
serum (data not shown). The individual patient sera should roughly reach the same max
HR value in response to anti-IgE in every performed PS Basophil HR.
4. Suﬃcient PMA/ionomycin response. The PMA/ionomycin values are often ≈100
ng/mL in HR, and should roughly be similar to the PMA/ionomycin response for the
optimal/super donor obtained in "Buﬀy Coat Screening" subsection 3.6. It is acknowl-
edged that the number of basophils can be decreased between 15-50 % over night (O/N)
and also be decreased due to centrifugation. Though, the basophil sensitivity was in-
creased largely by the IL-3 O/N, reaching higher values than PMA/ionomycin HR values
obtained from "Buﬀy Coat Screening".
3.8
Competitive Immunoassays
Before handling and testing the inhibitory eﬀect of the 14 FAST mCyp c 1 Post-sera, three
preliminary competitive model immunoassays were developed in order to obtain the thesis’
Competitive biological PS Basophil HR immunoassay (illustrated in Figure 8).
29
==PAGE:42==
3. METHODS
3.8.1
Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA (Rabbit Model and Human Model)
The ﬁrst model system to be designed and tested was the Competitive Gad c 1 direct sandwich
ELISA (referred to as Competitive ELISA) using either rabbit sera or the human Pre and Post-
sera containing IgG antibodies as a proof of concept of the inhibitory eﬀect of sIgG. The concept
of the Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA was based on the method described in subsection 3.5.
The theory behind the Competitive ELISA, was that the inhibitory sIgG in sera would be able
to bind Gad c 1 in the cod extract, thereby outcompete the possibility for free Gad c 1 to bind
to the pre-coated polyclonal rabbit anti-Gad c 1 in the well. Here, the higher the number of
sIgG-Gad c 1 binding complexes formed the weaker the ﬂuorescent signal.
In the rabbit system, the 3 sera dilutions were prepared for TAP 5, TAP 6 and NKS (neg-
ative control). The sera dilutions of 1%, 0.1 % to 0.01% were chosen and mixed with the cod
extract. These dilutions were based on the concentration of IgG and Gad c 1 present in the
serum sample and cod extract, respectively; TAP 5 having a concentration of 2.53 ng/mL (Terp
and Kostka, 2009) and Gad c 1 having a start concentration of 29 ng/mL (0.144 mg/mL diluted
5000 times). Using Avogadro constant and the molecular weights (IgG: 150 kDa and Gad c
1: 12 kDa) the amount of molecules present in the solutions were calculated. The cod extract
was calculated to contain 22×1010 Gad c 1 molecules and the sera dilutions: 1% ; 3×1013 IgG
molecules, 0.1% ; 3×1012 IgG molecules and 0.01 % ; 3×1011 IgG molecules. Having a mixture
of 1% sera and cod extract would theoretically have the best chance for inhibition since the
numbers of IgG molecules predominate over Gad c 1 molecules. A solution with the cod extract
and ELISA buﬀer were also included in the setup as a secondary negative control.
In the human system, the 14 Pre and Post-sera dilutions of 1%, 0.2 % and 0.1% and a
10-fold lower cod extract concentration (2.9 ng/mL) than for the rabbit system was chosen.
This concentration was used since it was experienced in Gad c 1 ELISA that the sIgG in the
human sera were less potent than the rabbit sera (obtained by Gad c 1 immunization), increas-
ing the chance for an equal competition and interpretation of the data. Like the rabbit model
system, a solution with the cod extract and ELISA buﬀer were also included in the setup as a
negative control.
The mixtures of cod extract and sera dilutions (rabbit and human sera) were pre-incubated
before proceeding to the method described in subsection 3.5, though the pre-incubated sam-
ples were now competing with the coating rabbit anti-Gad c 1 for Gad c 1 binding in the wells.
For interpretation of the results, the inhibitory eﬀects of using the rabbit sera and human sera
were calculated:
% Inhibition =

1 −ODPost- or TAP5/TAP6-sera −ODBackground
ODPre-sera or Cod 1 (rabbit model)


Figure 12: Scenario from Wells in Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA. The two diﬀerent expected responses of
the Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA using both the rabbit sera and human sera. 1) Well containing a lower amount
of Gad c 1-sIgG blocking antibodies either obtained from normal rabbit serum (NKS) or human Pre-sera. The
low Gad c 1 binding competition leads to a higher amount of Gad c 1 capable of binding to the coated rabbit
anti-Gad c 1 resulting in high color (orange) intensity giving high OD. 2) Well containing a higher amount of
Gad c 1-sIgG blocking antibodies either obtained from rabbits of TAP 5 and TAP 6 or human Post-sera. The high
