Based on the obtained knowledge from the competitive ELISA experiments, Competitive PS
Basophil HR immunoassay based models (rabbit and human) were developed.
3.8.2
Competitive PS Basophil HR (Rabbit Model)
As a proof of concept of the inhibitory serological eﬀect in relation to sIgG/sIgE ratio and
thereby β-parvalbumin competition, a biological model using rabbit sera was designed and
tested in a Competitive PS Basophil HR biological immunoassay.
The concept behind this rabbit model system, like in the Competitive ELISA, involve the
inhibitory sIgG antibodies contained in the rabbit sera. These sIgG would instead of competing
for Gad c 1 binding with the rabbit anti-Gad c 1 coated in the well, now compete with the sIgE
loaded on the basophils.
31
==PAGE:44==
3. METHODS
A low sera dilution was believed to induce multiple Gad c 1-sIgG binding, thereby block Gad c
1 from binding to sIgE-FcϵRI bound on basophils, resulting in reduced HR.
Based on the same procedure as in subsection 3.7, PS was performed with In-house sera,
to saturate the basophils (obtained by Buﬀy Coat Screening: subsection 3.6) with their ﬁsh
allergenic sIgE proﬁles. Simultaneously, TAP 6 and NKS (TAP 5 excluded) were mixed 1:1
with a constant concentration of cod extract (29 ng/mL), resulting in a ﬁnal dilution range
from 1 % to 10−6 % sera contained in the samples. The sera mixed with cod solution were
pre-incubated for 1 h., where Gad c 1-sIgG binding complexes were expected to be formed. As
positive controls for true inhibition point and thus to test for unspeciﬁc cell activation or plate
interference; TAP 6 and NKS were mixed 1:1 with pipes buﬀer. The cod extract was also mixed
with pipes buﬀer, as a positive control for no inhibitory substances present and thus a quality
control for assay performance. The detailed procedure can be seen in Appendix L.
After incubation, all TAP mixed with cod extract dilutions and fresh-made controls: anti-IgE
and PMA/ionomycin, were added to HI-plates followed by addition of cell suspension contain-
ing PS basophils with In-house sera. When adding the solutions to the wells, the Gad c 1-sIgG
binding complexes were expected to outcompete the chance for Gad c 1 binding to sIgE on
basophils, resulting in reduced HR compared to scenarios with no sera competition; wells con-
taining only cod extract and NKS (Figure 13). The histamine released were quantiﬁed in the
same manner as described in subsection 3.6.

==PAGE:45==
3. METHODS
3.8.3
Competitive PS Basophil HR (FAST-sera)
Based on the acquired knowledge and experience from the preliminary model immunoassays,
the thesis’ Competitive PS Basophil HR immunoassay was designed and tested using Pre- and
Post-sera from the FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 vaccination.
The theory behind the biological competition was based on the proposed mechanism in subsub-
section 1.2.2. The sIgG blocking antibodies, primarily IgG4, towards native β-parvalbumin
(such as cod and carp) should be increased in Post-sera after few months of FAST ﬁsh mCyp c
1 treatment, inducing their inhibitory eﬀect by binding to β-parvalbumins before reaching sIgE
on the basophils and/or by direct basophils inhibition Figure 14.
The Competitive PS Basophil HR experiments with the FAST-sera were designed to evaluate
the reduced level of HR induced by the Post-sera compared to the Pre-sera. The procedure was
based on the concept described in subsubsection 3.8.2, though rabbit sera were now replaced
with human sera and the allergen rCyp c 1 was included as well in a concentration of 5 ng/mL.
The cod extract concentration was now changed in the setup to a concentration of 2880 ng/mL.
As negative controls for inhibition, the WE pool, cod extract and rCyp c 1 were mixed with
pipes buﬀer. The detailed procedure can be seen in Appendix L.
Before spending too much sera samples from the FAST study, PS Basophil HR was ﬁrst con-
ducted as test trials. Firstly, a test trial with PS using Pre-sera based on few selected patients
was conducted to verify whether Competitive PS Basophil HR was possible to be conducted
with human sera from the FAST study. Furthermore, In-house sera were used to test further
dilutions and to investigate the inhibition window and inhibition trend based on few chosen
patient sera.
Finally, PS Basophil HR was conducted with both the Pre-sera and the Post-sera from all the
patients to challenge the PS proﬁle with corresponding competitive sera samples; Pre-sera and
Post-sera, to evaluate on the inhibitory eﬀectiveness achieved from the Post-sera. When analyz-
ing the change in HR, the %HR ratio between Post- over Pre-sera was calculated (%HRPost/Pre)
together with the inhibition in percentage:
%InhibtionPost/Pre =

1 −%HR PostSera
%HR PreSera

· 100
(4)
Both scenarios of PS with Pre-sera and PS with Post-sera were performed. The PS with Pre-sera
was believed to be more robust and ideal system for representing the IgG blocking/inhibitory
eﬀect since the Pre-sera samples have a purer serological proﬁle representing the full allergic
sIgE proﬁle. Whereas, a PS with Post-sera samples represent a more biological relevant pro-
cedure, representing the biological proﬁle achieved from vaccinated ﬁsh allergic patients after
withdrawal of vaccine.
33
==PAGE:46==
3. METHODS
Since the Post-sera are not washed away from cell suspension after PS, the presence of IgG
antibodies in the cell suspension could interfere with the competitive samples: Pre-/Post-sera
in mixture with the allergens, thereby blur the IgG blocking/inhibitory eﬀect induced by these
competitive samples. Even so, it was believed that using PS with Post-sera would reduce the
HR in a higher degree than PS with Pre-sera and also result in a higher %HR ratio between
the Pre- and Post-sera samples mixed with β-parvalbumin (%HRPost/Pre).
The diﬀerent scenarios in the wells of Competitive PS Basophil HR using both Pre-sera and
Post-sera are illustrated in Figure 14.
Fish parvalbumin-sIgE allergic profile 
(FcεRI saturated with sIgE)
Fish parvalbumin-sIgE allergic profile
(FcεRI saturated with sIgE)
Fish parvalbumin-sIgG/sIgE allergic profile
Fish parvalbumin-sIgG/sIgE allergic profile
Figure 14: The Diﬀerent Scenarios of Competitive PS Basophil HR (Human Model). The PS
basophils will be fully saturated with either Pre- or Post-sera. The four diﬀerent scenarios display the proposed
basophil HR. 1.1) PS with Pre-sera challenged with Pre-sera mixed with β-parvalbumin. 1.2) PS with Pre-sera
challenged with Post-sera mixed with β-parvalbumin. 2.1) PS with Post-sera challenged with Pre-sera mixed with
β-parvalbumin. 2.2) PS with Post-sera challenged with Post-sera mixed with β-parvalbumin. β-parvalbumin:
Gad c 1 or rCyp c 1. The sIgE (green antibodies) and the inhibitory substances (orange antibodies): IgG1/3 and
IgG4.

3. METHODS
3.9
Histamine Release - A Dose-Response Curve
Measuring basophil HR, a dose-response curve should be obtained for accurate interpretation of
basophil sensitivity and reactivity. Yielding a dose-response curve, require a serial of stimulant
dilutions, illustrated as a S-shaped curve.
The peak of the curve deﬁnes maximal basophil
reactivity, thus the maximal amount of histamine that can be released upon allergen exposure.
Whereas, the slope deﬁnes the basophil sensitivity; the lower the allergen concentration needed
to induce a signiﬁcant response, the higher the sensitivity (Figure 15)(Hamilton, 2010).
The sensitivity is determined by 1/2 max and onset, whereas the 1/2 max refers to the allergen
concentration required to produce 50 % of the response of Ymax and the onset; the allergen
concentration corresponding to the intercept and the background. The reactivity is determined
by AUC and Ymax, whereas AUC (area under the curve) is the area between the curve and the
background and Ymax, the maximum basophil response (Figure 15).
Figure 15: Visualization of Curve Parameters. The curve deﬁnes maximal basophil reactivity, indicated
by the highest peak, whereas the ascending trend (the slope) deﬁnes the basophil sensitivity. Basophil sensitivity
and reactivity are determined by the visualized parameters: AUC, Ymax,1/2maxand Onset.
3.10
Statistics
Every diluted sample was performed in duplicates in each immunoassay to obtain statistically
values. Excel was used for calculations (HR-values, %HR-values, 3-parameter curve (Sigmoid
curves). GraphPad Prism software (GraphPad Software, San Diego, Calif) was used for graph
and P-value generation (the null hypothesis is rejected when p < 0.05 and not rejected when p
> 0.05) and to calculate correlations.
For calculating the correlation, the non-parametric tool; Spearman’s rank correlations coeﬃcient
(rs) was used with no tied rank, which measures the strength and direction of the monotonic
association between two variables; the closer rs is to +1 the stronger the monotonic relationship
(Altman, 1992).
rs = 1 −
6 P d2
i
n(n2 −1)
(5)
d denotes the diﬀerence between ranks (determined by math or english) and n the sample size.

4. RESULTS
4.1
Cod Extract Validation
4.1.1
Gad c 1 ELISA
Before designing the PS Basophil HR and the competitive chemical/biological immunoassays,
cod extracts were produced and validated for the content of Gad c 1 by performing a Gad c 1
Direct Sandwich ELISA. Pure rCyp c 1 was included in the setup to investigate crossreactivity
between the two ﬁsh species.

Figure 17: β-Parvalbumin Content of Cod 1, Cod 2, & rCyp c 1. The X-axis (logarithmic scale base
10), the dilution of samples containing Gad c 1 (3-fold dilutions ranging from: 1.0×10−2 to 2.8×10−8. The
Y-axis, OD at 490 nm (Ref. 630 nm) reﬂecting the level of Gad c 1 bound. R2 and EC50 values are calculated
by the 3-polynomial model in GraphPad Prism. The background (blank) was calculated to OD 0.067.
As seen in Figure 17 it was possible to produce cod extracts containing Gad c 1 parvalbumin
from Cod powder 1 and 2. The two cod extracts were potent and generate desired dose-response
"S" curves with high R2 values (0.99), all reaching a plateau at the lowest dilution.
rCyp c 1 was as well able to generate a dose-response curve, indicating its ability to bind anti-
Gad c 1 in the assay even though the anti-Gad c 1 antibodies have higher speciﬁcity to Gad c 1
than rCyp c 1. This veriﬁed the crossreactivity found between the two ﬁsh species as described
in the introduction (rCyp c 1 has 68 % sequence homology with Gad c 1) (Table 1).
Even though crossreactivity between cod and carp was observed, a low eﬃcacy (maximum eﬀect
of the allergen) and a diﬀerent curve pattern (no parallelism with the Cod curves) was observed
for rCyp c 1 compared to the cod extracts, which was not as expected. Opposite rCyp c 1, Cod
1 reached the highest maximum eﬀect, having a higher OD-value of 1.3 at the plateau compared
to Cod 2 and rCyp c 1, having OD-values of 1.2 and 0.65, respectively.
Cod 1 showed as well the highest potency with a EC50 (deﬁned here as the 50% of a maximal
eﬀect) of 1.899×10−5 compared to both rCyp c 1 and Cod 2 with EC50 values of 1.923×10−5
and 3.63×10−5, respectively (Figure 17). Considering the diﬀerence in eﬃcacy between Cod
1 and Cod 2, Cod powder 1 might contain a higher parvalbumin concentration than the Cod
powder 2, but since no Gad c 1 standard was available for the ELISA, the Cod 1 parvalbumin
37
==PAGE:50==
4. RESULTS
concentration could not be calculated. From a study performed here at LMA by Terp and
Kostka (2009), the Gad c 1 concentration in the cod extract was estimated to 0.144 mg/mL. In
further experiments, this concentration was used as a reference for Cod 1 calculations.
Since powder from Cod 1 showed both higher potency and eﬃcacy than Cod 2, Cod 1 (batch#
1) was reproduced in larger amounts to batch# 2 (Cod 1.2) used in further experiments. Cod
1.2 was quality ensured by the Gad c 1 ELISA.

as well, PS Basophil HR was performed with three In-house sera (2031-23, 1362-57 and 1983-19)
and WE pool as the negative serum control (Figure 18).

In-house Sera and Allergen Reactivity.
PS Basophil HR performed with three In-house

As illustrated in Figure 18, all In-house sera were able to generate dose-response curves af-
ter allergen stimulation. For stimulation with cod extract, desired dose-response curves were
observed with the chosen concentration range, opposite rCyp c 1 which had too high a con-
centration of the pure allergen; making it impossible to determine the sensitivity. Based on
these results, the concentration range of rCyp c 1 was lowered 1000-fold in the remaining PS
experiments.
In regards to PS Basophil HR feasibility, In-house sera 1362-57 and 1983-19 responded with
max %HR of ≈75 compared to 2031-23 which generated a max %HR of ≈40, as expected from
their corresponding sIgE values (subsection 3.4). By testing all three sera multiple times in
diﬀerent PS Basophil HR set-ups (data not shown), sera from 1362-57 showed to be most stable
and was therefore used as quality control sera in all PS experiments forward.
The results showed how PS Basophil HR was manageable with In-house sera and the ﬁsh par-
valbumins: Gad c 1 (cod extract) and rCyp c 1 were reactive in the biological immunoassay,
allowing PS Basophil HR with the FAST-sera to be stimulated with the respective allergens.

==PAGE:53==
4. RESULTS
As illustrated in Figure 20, almost all patient sera (besides sera from P3) were able to generate
dose-response curves with high reactivity after cod extract and rCyp c 1 stimulation and thus
feasible to use in PS Basophil HR. This correlates roughly with sIgE levels measured by the
ImmunoCAP® system (Figure 19). P3 belonging to CAP class 1 did not have the ability
to mediate basophil HR upon allergen stimulation, due to %HR values below the cut-oﬀlevel.
P6 and P16 %HR levels had reduced reactivity compared to the other patient sera since they
elicit responses just above cut-oﬀ. Interestingly, these patients belonged to CAP class 3 with
sIgE of 22.1 and 11.8 ng/mL, respectively. This indicates that using a biochemical system such
as measuring sIgE by the ImmunoCAP® system does not necessarily correlates with values
obtained by a biological system. All the other patients belonging to CAP class 3 followed the
S-shaped curve trend, but with remarkable variation in magnitude and trend, constituting the
transition state between weak responses generated in CAP class 2 to strong responses in CAP
class 4. On the opposite, patients belonging to CAP class 4 mediated more identical clustered
%HR values.
Even though sIgE levels were not available for rCyp c 1, the curve trend for every patient ﬁt
the curve trend for cod extract, indicating crossreactivity.
As the results are expressed as max %HR using PMA/ionomycin it was expected to reach values
of maximum 100% HR. Interestingly, patients belonging to CAP class 4 showed a release above
100%. This indicated that the cod extract and rCyp c 1 were able to stimulate more eﬃcient
responses compared to the chemical substance PMA/ionomycin and thus reﬂect the allergic
response in a higher degree.
4.1.3.2
PS Basophil HR performed with Post-Sera
As for PS with Pre-sera, PS with Post-sera were conducted to test whether the patient sera
were feasible to use in PS Basophil HR. Using Post-sera instead of Pre-sera reﬂect the new
reduced allergenic proﬁle obtained after mCyp c 1 treatment. Therefore, it was the believe that
a reduced %HR would be observed performing PS with Post-sera compared to Pre-sera.
The %HR levels after PS with Post-sera for all 14 patients are visualized in Figure 21 according
to their respective CAP classes (Figure 19). In the setup, WE pool was included as the negative
serum control (not shown on the ﬁgure since it was below cut-oﬀ) and all values above cut-oﬀ
(10 %HR) indicated a positive response.

c 1 treatment has the ability to dampen the allergic response, resulting in a reduced release of
histamine.
42
==PAGE:55==
4. RESULTS
In regards to the sIgE serum level against codﬁsh measured by the ImmunoCAP® system
before mCyp c 1 treatment, three patients (P3, P10, P11) managed to shift CAP classes after
mCyp c 1 treatment. P3 was observed to induce more sIgE, opposite P10 and P11 inducing
less sIgE after treatment (Figure 19). Compared to the PS with Pre-sera, P3 was now able to
mediate a response of approximately 30 %HR, moving the patient into CAP class 3, enabling
suﬃcient PS. In regards to P10 and P11, PS with Post-sera showed to be highly feasible with
%HR peak levels of ≈90 %HR and ≈80 %HR, respectively. Three patient sera: P6, P7 and P13
were detected near or under the cut-oﬀlevel in PS with Post-sera, having a reduced reactivity.
The rest of the FAST-sera were observed to be feasible in performing PS. This indicated that
sera from P7, P13 and especially P6, might not be suﬃcient enough to obtain representative
results on forward.
The level of %HR for all individual patients using both Pre- and Post-sera were used further on
in Competitive PS Basophil HR assays as an indication for their inhibiting capacity.
4.2
Proof of Concept of the Inhibitory IgG Eﬀect (Rabbit Model)
This rabbit model system assessed in the Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA, was developed to test
and validate whether IgG antibodies in general, here IgG from rabbit sera, could be used as
a competitive and therefore an inhibitory tool for Gad c 1 (contained in the cod extract) binding.
The concept was to use a constant cod (Gad c 1) concentration from where inhibition was
measured. The cod concentration was identiﬁed to be 29 ng/mL as determined in subsubsec-
tion 3.8.1. The cod constant of 29 ng/mL was mixed with either TAP 5 (2.53 mg/mL IgG
pooled fraction) and TAP 6 (1.72 mg/mL IgG pooled fraction) in three diﬀerent sera dilutions.
From this Competitive ELISA experiment it was expected to obtain diﬀerent inhibition levels
correlated to the present amount of sIgG: the higher the amount of sIgG present, the higher the
inhibition. In the setup, NKS was included as the negative serum control.
43

Figure 22: Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA - 1h. vs. Over Night (O/N). The X-axis, three diﬀerent sera
dilutions; 1:100 = 1 % sera, 1:1000 = 0.1% sera, 1:10000 = 0.01 %. The Y-axis, the % inhibition level, where
Cod 1 (1h. and O/N) mixed with buﬀer is the reference for 0% inhibition. Blue lines: TAP 5 + Cod 1. Pink
lines: TAP 6 + Cod 1. Grey lines: NKS+Cod 1. Raw OD-values can be visualized in Appendix G.
From the TAP 5 and TAP 6 curves in the graph (Figure 22) the total inhibition window
ranging from around 0% (1:10000), ≈50% (1:1000), and 100% (1:100) was easily observed. In
the lowest dilution point, 100 % inhibition of cod extract (Gad c 1) was observed indicating
high amount of sIgG for both TAP 5 and TAP 6. In the highest dilution point, 0 % inhibition
of Gad c 1 was observed indicating a low amount of sIgG. In regards to TAP 5 at 1:1000 di-
lution, both pre-incubations with 1 hour and O/N, the % level of inhibition (calculated from
Equation 3) were generally a bit higher compared to TAP 6, which correspond with the sIgG
levels measured by Terp and Kostka (2009), in which TAP 5 had a higher sIgG level than TAP
6 subsection 3.1. This could indicate the TAP 5 sera would be a bit better tool for inhi-
bition in further experiments. Furthermore, the pre-incubation times: 1h. and O/N, for the
inhibitory samples were also investigated. O/N pre-incubations for TAP 5 mixed with Cod 1 and
TAP 6 mixed with Cod 1 had roughly 11 % higher inhibitory eﬀect than 1 h. pre-incubations
at 1:1000 dilution point, but no solid diﬀerence was observed for 1:100 and 1:10000 sera di-
lutions. Therefore, it was not worth to perform O/N pre-inbubations, since it would extend
the experimental time frame in all the further experiments. The negative control composed of
NKS worked ﬁne, since the curve was almost constant. NKS could actually inhibit ≈<12 %,
thus no crucial inhibitory eﬀect exist. The small inhibition eﬀect could indicate that NKS have
some natural occurring IgG able to bind the cod extract or that unspeciﬁc binding had occurred.
To summarize, there was no doubt that it was possible to use the rabbit sera containing sIgG
against Gad c 1 as an inhibitory tool. It was satisfying to see how 1 h. pre-incubation was enough
time to obtain the entire inhibition window. On these accounts, the rabbit sera dilutions; 1:100
and 1:10000 were directly transferred into PS Basophil HR in the next subsection 4.3.
44
==PAGE:57==
4. RESULTS
4.3
Proof of Concept of the Inhibitory IgG/IgE Eﬀect (Rabbit model)
Before performing Competitive PS Basophil HR with rabbit IgG, cod extract stability was tested
beforehand, to ensure that no degradation of β-parvalbumin would occur during incubation
with TAP/NKS when performing Competitive PS Basophil HR. The cod extract dilutions were
incubated in 1h. at three conditions: RT (21 ◦C, freshly made), 8 ◦C and 37 ◦C and added to
cell suspensions. PS with all three In-house sera were performed (data only shown for 1362-57.
Data for 2031-23 and 1983-19 can be found in Appendix C).

Figure 23: Cod Stability Testing. The X-axis, the concentration of allergen (cod extract) in ng/mL (10-fold

As illustrated in Figure 23 (and in Appendix C), β-parvalbumin was not degraded when
incubated at 37 ◦C, as expected according to the theory. Furthermore, no diﬀerence between
RT (21 ◦C), 8 ◦C and 37 ◦C was observed in regards to reactivity, all reaching ≈60%HR at the
highest concentration. In regards to sensitivity, samples incubated at RT (21 ◦C) had a higher
sensitivity: responding at 100 ng/mL compared to 8 ◦C and 37 ◦C ﬁrst responding at 1000
ng/mL. However, this diﬀerence was not of value since the RT concentration (100 ng/mL) was
near cut-oﬀ(10 %HR).
After cod stability ensured at 37 ◦C, Competitive PS Basophil HR assay using rabbit IgG sera
(TAP 6) was developed to assess whether it was possible to retrieve the same inhibition level
towards the cod extract with rabbit IgG sera in a biological system as observed in Competitive
Gad c 1 ELISA (Figure 22).
This PS Basophil HR assay using rabbit IgG sera was performed using TAP dilutions (1:100 =
1 % sera, 1:10.000 = 0.01 %, 1:1.000.000 = 0.0001% sera) mixed with a constant concentration
of cod (mixed with pipes buﬀer) to obtain diﬀerent inhibition levels correlated to the present
amount of sIgG. TAP 6 was used as the inhibitory sera instead of TAP 5, since this sera per-
formed best in PS Basophil HR assays (Data not shown).

==PAGE:58==
4. RESULTS
Since ELISA and PS Basophil HR are two diﬀerent test systems, the dilutions were increased
compared to the ELISA setup and the cod extract concentration was as well increased to 10.000
ng/mL based on peaks observed in Figure 20. The PS was in this setup performed on all
In-house sera with TAP 6 as the inhibiting sera (data only shown for 1362-57. Data for 2031-23
and 1983-19 can be found in Appendix D), and the cod extract and NKS were used as the
negative controls (Figure 24).

Figure 24: Rabbit Inhibition Model. The X-axis, three diﬀerent sera dilutions (1:100 = 1% sera, 1:10.000
= 0.01%, 1:1.000.000 = 0.001% sera). The Y-axis, basophil %HR calculated based on max. PMA/ionomycin

Using rabbit IgG sera in the Competitive PS Basophil HR assay rendered an inhibition level
almost as high as in the Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA, with an inhibition percentage of 81.7 %
at TAP dilution 1:100 using NKS as an inhibition reference (calculated by Equation 4). This
implied that TAP 6 was able to bind the Gad c 1 before Gad c 1 was able to crosslink the
sIgE loaded on basophils, which is necessary for inducing an HR. In dilution point: 1:10.000
(3×1011 IgG molecules) no inhibition was obtained in TAP 6 compared to NKS, which match
the expectation derived from ELISA and the fact that too few IgG in the sera were present to
inhibit crosslinking to the sIgE. Interestingly, at TAP dilution 1:1.000.000 an inhibition trend
(46.7 % inhibition) was observed again creating a "bell-shaped" curve. This trend was not ex-
pected since this dilution point contained 100 fold lower concentration of TAP 6 than the second
dilution point (1:10000) and thus should give a lower inhibition level, making the cod extract
dominant and the rabbit IgG sera submissive. Big cod aggregates/superantigens inducing IgG
immunocomplexes were suspected to be the reason for this bell-shaped trend. The same trend
was observed for the rest of the In-house sera: 1983-19 and 2031-23, see Appendix D.
46
==PAGE:59==
4. RESULTS
The fact that very low levels of inhibiting substances should be present in NKS (observed
in ELISA) and no inhibiting substance in the cod extract, created the expectation that both
NKS and the cod extract should reach the same high level of %HR.
As illustrated in Figure 24, this was not the case since the cod extract had a lower %HR
level than both TAP 6 at dilution 1:10.000 and NKS at all dilutions. The low cod %HR level
could be explained by the unspeciﬁc bindings observed when testing the rabbit sera: TAP 6
and NKS (≈13 ng/mL HR) in the HI-plate without cell suspension (Appendix E). This un-
speciﬁc bindings indicate some kind of serum interference in the assay. Due to this diﬀerence
between cod extract and NKS, the cod extract was only used to validate assay performance like
PMA/ionomycin and anti-IgE, thus was excluded in the following PS graphs.
Since an optimal inhibition window of 0-82 % was observed at dilution 1:100 to 1:10.000, it
was possible to proceed forward, designing a human model with the FAST-sera to repeat and
verify the results obtained by the rabbit model.
4.4
Proof of Concept of the Inhibitory IgG Eﬀect (Human Model)
In this human model, a Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA was developed and assessed to test whether
the 14 human Post-sera from the FAST study were able to be used as inhibitory tools and to
validate how good the sIgG blocking eﬀect induced by Post-sera were compared to the Pre-sera.
Furthermore, it was investigated if the patients sIgG level (sIgG/sIgG4Post/Pre) against Gad c 1
obtained from the ImmunoCAP® system correlated with obtained results in this Competitive
Gad c 1 ELISA (OD-valuesPost/Pre).
Before designing the Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA, the sIgG and sIgG4 levels raised against
Gad c 1 quantiﬁed by ImmunoCAP® system, were acknowledged to give an indication of the
relationship between the levels of Pre- versus Post-sera (Figure 25) (unpublished results from
FAST project, provided by Lars K. Poulsen). Many patient’s Post-sera had increased IgG/IgG4
levels against Gad c 1 compared to Pre-sera, except for P4, P6, and P12. Based on this immuno-
chemical quantiﬁcation it was anticipated from the qualitative measurements obtained from this
ELISA to see an increased blocking eﬀect induced by the Post-sera due to the increased levels
of sIgG and especially sIgG4.

Figure 25: sIgG and sIgG4 Levels Measured against Gad c 1. The X-axis, patients, where Pre indicate

From the acquired knowledge obtained in the Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA using rabbit sera; 1 h.
pre-incubation, cod extract at 14.4 ng/mL, and identical sera-dilutions were directly translated
into the human model performed with few selected patient sera. The results showed no diﬀerence
in responses, since the OD-values were almost identical for all dilution points (data not shown).
These results indicated either that a higher sIgG concentration was present in the rabbit sera
compared to the human sera or that sIgG from the rabbit sera had higher speciﬁcity and aﬃnity
against Gad c 1, opposite human sIgG sera, having lower speciﬁcity and aﬃnity against Gad c
1 due to a broader speciﬁcity towards other ﬁsh β-parvalbumin than only Gad c 1.
Subsequently, the cod extract concentration was reduced to 1.44 ng/mL with new sera-dilutions;
1%, 0.2 %, and 0.1 % (matching the ﬁnal sera-dilutions in Competitive PS Basophil HR using
the FAST-sera subsubsection 4.5.2).
After the ELISA was accomplished, the expected increase in blocking eﬀect from the Post-sera
(lowered OD-values) were obtained for most patients at dilution point 1:100 (1% sera), evaluated
and illustrated in Figure 26.

Figure 26: OD Levels in Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA (Human Model). The X-axis, patients (P).
Y-axis, OD values measured at 490nm. The bar chart illustrating the OD-values induced from Pre (red)- and

The ELISA set-up was performed using two plates, therefore illustrated in two bar charts due to
plate variance. The bar charts (Figure 26) demonstrate a diﬀerence between Pre- and Post-sera
after Gad c 1 stimulation and a variation in patient response exist. Some Pre-sera, especially P2
and P15, had exceptional low OD-values from the start when analyzing their Pre-sera compared
to the others and the Cod control. For P2 and P15 this were consistent with the high content
of sIgG4 against Gad c 1 in their Pre-sera, indicating that the Pre-sera were able to bind to
some of the Gad c 1, thus block the binding to the coated anti-Gad c 1 antibodies. To examine
the diﬀerence between the Pre- and Post-sera, the Post/Pre ratio (OD-valuesPost/Pre) for each
individual patient sera were analyzed, to evaluate the eﬀectiveness of the blocking/inhibiting
eﬀect.
For some patients: P11, P12, P13, and P16, the OD values (Figure 26b) were almost identical
or a little bit higher than the Cod 1.1 control. In theory it should not be possible to have a
higher OD value than the cod extract, since the cod concentration was constant and no addi-
tional Gad c 1 was added to the sera samples. This variance could be due to bad pipetting
or vortexing. Another sensible reason could be sera interference. As seen in Figure 26 the
patients could be categorized in an upper, middle, and lower group in relation to their ability
to block/inhibit based on the ratio of OD-valuesPost/Pre as illustrated in Table 5.
P1, P3, P13, and P15 placed in the upper group (0.02-0.40) had really high IgG blocking/in-
hibitory eﬀects (60-98 % inhibition eﬀect).
49
==PAGE:62==
4. RESULTS
P2, P5, P7, P9, and P16, in the middle group (0.70-0.90) were able to inhibit with 10-30 %,
whereas the placebos (P4, P6, P11) acted truly as placebos and were therefore placed in the
lower group (0.98-1.12), since their blocking/inhibitory eﬀect were almost zero ((-)3-2.4 %).
Remarkably did P10 and P12 also generate values near placebo level. This was not expected
for P10 which generated high sIgG levels after mCyp c 1 immunotherapy (Figure 25).

Since the ImmunoCAP® system and ELISA both are methods based on immunochemical
properties, they were expected to have a mutual relationship.
To investigate in detail if
there were serological correlations between diﬀerence in sIgG levels from Pre- and Post-sera
(sIgG/sIgG4Post/pre) and OD-valuesPost/Pre, two plots were made to show their relationship Fig-
ure 27. A high negative logarithmic relationship was wanted in the plots, since the Post-sera
containing possibly more IgG inhibit the cod extract in a higher degree (lowered OD) than Pre-
sera, giving a relation where Pre > Post. Whereas, the sIgG/sIgGPost/pre measured (logarithmic
values) were preferred to give positive values indicating Post-sera contain more IgG or sIgG4
than the Pre-sera, resulting in a relation where Post > Pre.
In the ﬁrst correlation plot, correlating (Figure 27a) sIgGPost/Pre and OD-valuesPost/Pre, the
Spearman’s rank (rs) was calculated to -0.38, indicating a weak association in their relationship,
supported by the P-value of 0.184. This weak correlation was particularly due to the order of
P5, P9, P10, and P16, which in ELISA performed with a low to a medium inhibition level,
whereas measurements by the ImmunoCAP® system revealed a really high increase in sIgG
levels (high sIgG Post/Pre). The placebos were placed almost in the same order in both methods,
whereas P1, P3, P13, and P15 were identiﬁed in the upper group with the highest negative val-
ues in the ELISA (induced 83-98 % inhibitionPost/Pre), although belonging to the middle group
by ImmunoCAP measurements.

Figure 27: Correlation between sIgG/IgG4Post/Pre Quantiﬁed in ImmunoCAP® system and OD-
valuesPost/Pre Qualitatively Measured in Gad c 1 ELISA. X-axis, the logaritmic sIgG and IgG4 ratio

The correlation is evaluated by the Spearman’s rank correlations coeﬃcient (rs) and the P-value.
In the second plot with sIgG4Post/Pre (Figure 27b) the Spearmans rank (rs) was calculated to
-0.65 indicating a strong relationship (twice as high compared to correlation with sIgG), sup-
ported by a P-value of 0.014. Here, did sIgG4 correlate more with the obtained ELISA results
and identiﬁed P1, P3, and P13 in the upper group with highest diﬀerence in ratio; Post/Pre
and P5, P9, P10, and P16 in the middle group. These results followed the theory presuming
that sIgG4 antibodies are related to the blocking/inhibitory eﬀect in AIT.
To summarize, from the results obtained in the Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA there were no
doubt that is was possible to use human sera containing sIgG as inhibitory tools. In addition, it
was possible for some patients Post-sera to inhibit >80 % (P1, P3, P15) in comparison to their
Pre-sera. From the investigation of the correlations, there was a strong relationship between
higher increase of sIgG4 level (especially for P1, P3, P13) against Gad c 1 and a higher proba-
bility to induce a blocking/inhibition eﬀect against Gad c 1. The results supported the theory
that sIgG-Gad c 1 complex using human sera would be able to block Gad c 1 from binding to
sIgE on basophils, thus dampen the HR.
51
==PAGE:64==
4. RESULTS
4.5
Validation of the Inhibitory IgG/IgE Eﬀect (FAST-Sera)
Before designing and testing the Competitive PS Basophil HR assay using the individual patient
sera from the FAST study, the serum itself was tested in mixture with the cod extract in the
HI-plates to detect whether unspeciﬁc bindings to glassﬁbers were present.
As acknowledged in Appendix E, the same trend was observed for all patients with a solid
serum interference at the highest dilution (1:100, 1% sera) of 39 ± 3.2 ng/mL. Since no substan-
tial sera variance were observed between the individual patients, no correction and subtraction
were adjusted in the following PS Basophil HR assays.
4.5.1
Competitive PS Basophil HR Test Trial
When designing the Competitive PS Basophil HR human model, experiences obtained from the
rabbit models were used and incorporated. To test whether the bell-shape trend would appear
again as observed in the rabbit PS model and to assess whether any diﬀerence between Pre- and
Post sera existed when performing PS, a test trial was conducted. The test trial was performed
using PS with Pre-sera from few selected patient sera: P1, P2, P4, and P5 challenged with cod
extract in mixture with Pre- or Post-sera. The sera were selected based on their diﬀerent levels
of IgG and sIgG4 (Figure 28) (unpublished results from FAST project, provided by Lars K.
Poulsen), giving the entire spectra when choosing P1, P2, P4 (Pbo), and P5.

4. RESULTS
As seen on Figure 28, the level of sIgG and sIgG4 increased for all patients receiving mCyp c
1 immunotherapy. Patients inducing a high sIgG level after mCyp c 1 immunotherapy, induced
a high level of IgG4 as well, determined by a high Spearman correlation coeﬃcient of 0.84, as
seen in (subsection A.1).
When performing the test trial, it was expected that using a constant cod concentration mixed
with Pre- or Post-dilutions ranging from 1%-0.01%, would resolve the bell-shape and instead
create an exponential curve showing the entire inhibition window according to the amount of
sIgG and sIgG4 generated. The higher amount of sIgG, the higher inhibition level. A high
ratio was especially expected for P1 and in some degree P2, having the highest induction of
sIgGPost/Pre and sIgG4Post/Pre (Table 6). It was as well expected that P4 (Pbo) would not gen-
erate any diﬀerence between Pre- and Post-sera due to no change in level of sIgG, sIgG4, and
sIgE (Table 6).

If taken the sIgEPost/Pre into consideration, the HR-reduction might be dampened since both

was believed that the sIgE produced after the immunotherapy might be of lower aﬃnity, and
the sIgG or/and sIgG4 would dominate the response.

negative serum control, expected to be constant.

Figure 29: A Test Trial Conducted with P1, P2, P4 and P5. The X-axis, sera dilutions ranging from
1% to 0.01 % sera. The Y-axis, basophil %HR calculated based on maximum PMA/ionomycin levels. The red

As demonstrated in the rabbit model (subsection 4.3), an optimal inhibition window for di-
lution 1:100 to 1:1000 was observed in the test trial (Figure 29). The highest change between
Pre- and Post-sera was especially observed for P1 with a %HRPost/Pre ratio of 0.22 (77.6% inhi-
bition) at dilution 1:100. A low %HRPost/Pre was observed for P5 (49.1% inhibition) and no ratio
diﬀerence in %HRPost/Pre for P4. A high %HRPost/Pre was observed as well for P2 with a ratio
of 0.88 (11.7% inhibition), which was not as expected, due to its high levels of sIgG and sIgG4
(Table 6). As expected, these results indicated that even though the levels of sIgE were in-
creased after immunotherapy, they behave submissive compared to the induction of sIgG/sIgG4
levels. Actually, the results obtained in the test trial correlated roughly with the generation of
IgG4; P1 having the highest induction, followed by P2 and P5 and at last P4 (Table 6).
For all patients, the bell-shaped trend was detected again after Pre- and Post-dilution 1:1000.
Furthermore, the trend was not resolved when using FAST-sera remained the suspicion of the
generation of big cod extract aggregates inducing immunocomplexes making cod unable to
crosslink the sIgE loaded on the basophils.
54
==PAGE:67==
4. RESULTS
If in fact immunocomplexes were generated, the theory was that they would be resolved if
further dilutions were included, making the sIgG in the Post-sera highly submissive. Therefore
an experiment was conducted including three additional dilution points reaching a range from
1:100 to 1:106. For this purpose the In-house sera 1362-57 and 1983 were used (to limit the use
of the FAST-sera) for PS and challenged with mixes of either Pre- or Post-sera from patients:
P1, P2, P4 and P5. The results can be seen in Appendix F. Even though additional dilution
points were included in the setup, the bell-shape trend was not resolved, even though the ratio
between patient IgG sera and cod was substantially low, containing 3×109 IgG molecules at
dilution 1:106 compared to the 22×1010 Gad c 1 molecules.
Since the whole inhibition window was achieved when applying dilutions ranging from 1:100-
1:1000, it was decided to use this dilution interval, including an additional dilution point of
1:500 to increase the power of the setup, having sera dilutions of 1%, 0.2 %, and 0.1 %.
These new dilutions were evaluated using an identical assay setup as described for the test
trial, however with new patients: P1, P9, P10 and P11 (P1 was included again to include a
known %HR level reference). When taken the results for the test trial into consideration, it was
expected to see patients with the highest induction of sIgG4 would perform best, generating a
higher ratio between Pre- and Post-sera (sIgG4Post/Pre).

Figure 30: A Test Trial with New Dilutions. The X-axis, sera dilutions ranging from 1% to 0.1 % sera.
The Y-axis, basophil %HR calculated based on maximum PMA/ionomycin levels. The red line: mix of cod and
Pre-sera. The green line: mix of cod and Post-sera. The purple line: WE pool used as a negative serum control.

The ratio between Pre- and Post-sera was observed to be highest for P9 with a ratio of 0.57
(42.5 % inhibition), followed by P1 with a ratio of 0.73 (27.2% inhibition), at dilution 1:100. In
regards to P10 and P11, no inhibitions were observed at dilution 1:100 with ratios of 1 (≈0 %
inhibition). The fact that P1 and P9 had the highest Post/Pre ratio, implied that sIgG4 might
aﬀect the response in a higher degree than the other serological values.
Even though P1 had a low %HRPost/Pre in this setup (27.2 % inhibition), the %HRPost/Pre level
did not reach the same level as for the test trial with a ratio of (77.6 % inhibition). The higher
ratio obtained in the test trial was suspected to be due to donor variance. Since the assay with
optimal dilutions (Figure 30) were performed twice with low variance between the obtained
results, it was believed that this new setup represented a more true %HRPost/Pre.
In regards to the bell-shape trend observed in both Figure 24 and Figure 29, using the new
dilution window of 1%, 0.2 %, and 0.1 % sera, resolved the inhibition problem in such degree
that it was decided to continue with the main objective of this thesis: the development of a
biological PS Basophil HR immunoassay using human Pre-sera and Post-sera, to validate the
inhibitory serological eﬀect of IgG induced by mCyp c 1 immunotherapy.
56
==PAGE:69==
4. RESULTS
4.5.2
Competitive PS Basophil HR with Pre-Sera
In this assay, PS was conducted with Pre-sera to validate the allergic sIgE proﬁle before mCyp
c 1 immunotherapy. Having this allergic proﬁle and challenging it with Pre-sera and the com-
petitive sera; Post-sera both in solution with cod extract and rCyp c 1, would make it possible
to evaluate the real proposed biological mechanism of mCyp c 1 achieved from the Post-sera.
Using PS with Pre-sera in the competitive system gives a more pure system, where no or a
limited amount of inhibiting sIgG substances are present before adding the solutions of allergen
and sera.
When performing the Competitive PS Basophil HR assay, the criterion for an optimal donor
was fulﬁlled with a PMA/ionomycin level of 177 ng/mL and an anti-IgE level of 135 ng/mL (a
super donor in regards to anti-IgE). In the setup a constant cod and rCyp c 1 concentration
were mixed with Pre- and Post-sera (1%, 0.2 %, 0.1%) from the individual patients in the FAST
study.
Before performing the assay, it was expected that patients inducing the highest sIgGPost/Pre and
sIgG4Post/Pre towards codﬁsh (Figure 28), also would generate the highest ratio diﬀerence (low
%HRPost/Pre), since these Post-sera would be able to inhibit the system in a higher degree and
thus lower the HR. Even though no sIgG level was available for rCyp c 1, it was expected that
it followed the same pattern as for cod, due to their high crossreactivity.
After performing the assay, it was acknowledged that a ratio between Pre- and Post-sera only
was highly observed at sera dilution 1:100 as seen in Appendix H. Therefore, %HR levels
obtained after Competitive PS with Pre-sera challenged with Pre- or Post-sera were only visu-
alized with dilution 1:100 for the individual patients as seen in Figure 31. Data for P4 and
P11 was obtained from the test trial and P3 and P6 were excluded in the setup since they did
not reach the cut-oﬀlevel of 10 ng/mL.
57

Figure 31: Bar Chart: Competitive PS Basophil HR with Pre-sera. The X-axis, sera for each patient
obtained before (Pre: green) and after (Post: red) mCyp c 1 immunotherapy. The Y-axis, basophil %HR at sera
dilution 1:100 calculated based on maximum PMA/ionomycin levels. Pbo: placebo-treated patients. The value
above each patient Pre and Post bars, indicate the ratio between the Pre- and Post-sera after PS with Pre-sera;
the closer the value is to 1, the smaller the diﬀerence between Pre and Post-sera and vice versa. For (a) and (b):
P9 and P13 Pre-sera are above cut-oﬀlevel but their Post-sera are below, thus no %HR ratio can be calculated.
As visualized in Figure 31, the increased amount of sIgG and sIgG4 present in the Post-
sera reduced the HR response for all patients (besides P11 when using the cod extract). This
indicated that the IgG antibodies within the Post-sera were able to bind both the cod extract
and rCyp c 1 in some degree before reaching the sIgE loaded on the basophils, resulting in a
reduced HR.
When stimulating with cod extract, a low %HRPost/Pre was observed for P12 (60.6% inhibition),
P15 (45.4% inhibition), P7 (40.5% inhibition), P16 (37.1% inhibition) and P1 (35.7% inhibition)
(green group in Table 8). If comparing these data with the ratio of sIgG measured before
and after immunotherapy, the expectations were fulﬁlled when looking at P12 and P16, since
these patients also generated some of the highest sIgGPost/Pre towards codﬁsh; 108.0 and 31.9
respectively (Figure 28). Instead, if comparing the data with the ratio of sIgG4 measured
before and after immunotherapy, P1 and P7 matched the level (Figure 28). For P15 both a
high ratio of sIgG and sIgG4 were induced, ranking the patient together with the P1, P7, P12,
and P16. Thus, inducing a high amount of sIgG and/or sIgG4 blocking antibodies, outcompete
cod or rCyp c 1 for binding to sIgE, resulting in reduced HR. The fact that the placebo-treated
patients (P4 and P11) had a equal %HRPost/Pre of 0.99 and 1.01 respectively was as expected,
indicating no eﬀect of immunotherapy (orange group in Table 8).
A similar pattern as for the cod extract was observed when stimulating with rCyp c 1 in regards
to P12 and P16 (Table 8). Interestingly, the response towards rCyp c 1 seemed dampen for all
patients.

As observed in Figure 31, the %HRPost/Pre was observed to be substantially lower using the cod
extract than using rCyp c 1, which was not as expected. It was believed that rCyp c 1 would
generate higher or a similar %HR response due to the fact that the patients were vaccinated
with a modiﬁed version of rCyp c 1; mCyp c 1 and cod and carp showed some crossreactivity
(Figure 3). To resolve whether a correlation was indeed detected between the cod extract and
rCyp c 1 (Figure 32) Spearman’s correlation coeﬃcient was applied. Patient: 3, 4, 6, 9, and 13
were excluded in the correlation plot since these patients did not have Pre-sera or/and Post-sera
values above cut-oﬀwhen stimulating with cod extract or rCyp c 1.

==PAGE:72==
4. RESULTS
As seen in the correlation plot Figure 32, a moderate association with a rs of 0.42 between the
change in %HRPost/Pre using the cod extract in relation to rCyp c 1 was observed. Even though
a moderate association was observed, the correlation was not signiﬁcant with a P-value of 0.28.
In the plot, 4 groups were roughly produced: 1) P16 having a moderate response towards both
the cod extract and rCyp c 1, 2) P12 having the highest response towards cod extract and a
moderate response towards rCyp c 1, 3) P1, P7, P15 having responses as high as P16 towards
cod extract and almost no response towards rCyp c 1 and 4) P2, P5 and P11 having almost no
response towards both rCyp c 1 and the cod extract. These results implied that every single
individual responding diﬀerently to diﬀerent ﬁsh epitopes and crossreactivity mostly occur due
to the observed relationship. However, it should be noticed that only 9 patients were included
in the correlation, possibly lowering the power of the correlation.
After analyzing the %HRPost/Pre for all patients in Figure 31, the patients were correlated with
their individual serological sIgGPost/Pre and sIgG4Post/Pre levels obtained by the ImmunoCAP®
system (Figure 28). This was applied to identify whether inducing a high amount of serological
sIgG4 or IgG antibodies after mCyp c 1 immunotherapy were correlated with the reduced HR
observed after mCyp c 1 immunotherapy.

sera.The X-axis, the log value of a) sIgGPost/Pre or b) sIgG4Post/Pre level for each patient. The Y-axis, the log
value of %HRPost/Pre for each patient. In the plot, the sIgGPost/Pre and sIgG4Post/Pre raised against codﬁsh are

As illustrated in Figure 33a, a moderate association of rs of -0.50 (P value of 0.14, insigniﬁcant)
was observed when correlating %HRPost/Pre with sIgGPost/Pre and an even higher association was
observed when correlating %HRPost/Pre with sIgG4Post/Pre giving a rs of -0.79 (P-value 0f 0.008,
signiﬁcant) as seen in Figure 33b.
60
==PAGE:73==
4. RESULTS
Particularly this mutual relationship implied that the biochemical ImmunoCAP® system and
the biological Basophil HR assay predict similar tendencies; generating a high amount of sIgG
antibodies after mCyp c 1 immunotherapy matches a highly reduced HR after mCyp c 1 im-
munotherapy. This was especially observed, when analyzing the correlation with sIgG4Post/Pre
compared to sIgGPost/Pre. When correlating sIgG4Post/Pre with %HRPost/Pre, two groups were
formed; group 1 with P1, P7, P12, P15 and P16 and group 2 with P2, P4, P5, P10, P11. Both
groups matched the expectations; inducing a high amount of sIgG4 results in a high Post/Pre
ratio and vice versa. This implied that patients belonging to group 1 might respond better to
mCyp c 1 immunotherapy than group 2 if taken the theory about sIgG4 working as neutralizing
antibodies into account.
Thus, using the patient’s antibody proﬁle before immunotherapy by performing Competitive
PS Basophil HR assay using Pre-sera, enabled us to visualize how the individual patient re-
sponded to the treatment; producing inhibiting IgG antibodies with high speciﬁcity towards
codﬁsh capable of inhibiting or reducing the allergic response. Analyzing the data obtained,
indicated that P12 and P16 and to some degree P1, P7 and P15 have beneﬁted from mCyp c1
immunotherapy.
4.5.3
Competitive PS Basophil HR with Post-Sera
At last but not least, a more biological relevant procedure performing PS with Post-sera (new
sIgG/sIgE proﬁle), representing the daily life of vaccinated ﬁsh allergic patients after withdrawal
of vaccine, was investigated.
When performing the Competitive PS Basophil HR assay with Post-sera, the criterion for a
super donor was fulﬁlled with a PMA/ionomycin level of 286 ng/mL and an anti-IgE level of
131 ng/mL. In the setup P6 was excluded since this serum was unable to mediate a response
above cut-oﬀin the PS with Post-sera (paragraph 4.1.3.2). After conducting PS with the
13 Post-sera, the basophils were challenged with cod extract and rCyp c 1 in solution with the
competitive sera samples from 13 Post-sera (primarily sIgG/sIgE) and the 13 Pre-sera (primarily
sIgE/IgG).
The interesting with this set-up was to directly compare the results with the PS conducted
with Pre-sera, to investigate if they performed in a similar way, which method could reduced
the most HR and analyze which method correlated best with sIgG/sIgG4Post/Pre obtained from
ImmunoCAP® system.
Based on PS with Post-sera it was expected to achieve higher HR reduction between Pre- and
Post-sera than observed for PS with Pre-sera. After performing the assay, it was acknowledged
that a diﬀerence between Pre- and Post-sera only was observed at sera dilution 1:100 (the
similar trend as for PS performed with Pre-sera) as seen in Appendix I. Therefore, %HR
levels obtained after Competitive PS with Pre-sera challenged with Pre- or Post-sera were only
visualized with dilution 1:100 for the individual patients in Figure 34.

Firstly, by looking at the bar charts in Figure 34 and Table 9, the cod extract was generally
more responsive compared to rCyp c 1, showing a higher ratio between Pre- and Post-sera. The
same pattern was obtained for PS with Pre-sera, supporting the dampened trend for rCyp c 1
(subsubsection 4.5.2).

extract, four patients were identiﬁed with low %HRPost/Pre values (green group) (Table 9): P9
(62.3 % inhibitionPost/Pre), P1 (58.5 % inhibitionPost/Pre), P15 (43.8 % inhibitionPost/Pre), and P7
(36.1 % inhibitionPost/Pre). These patients had the most eﬀective sera inducing highest inhibitory
eﬀect. By comparing these data with sIgG versus sIgG4 measured against codﬁsh before and
after immunotherapy, the expectations from the theory were fulﬁlled since these patients had
generated the highest increase in sIgG4Post/Pre. Especially, P7 and P9 had 6.9 and 2.9 times
higher IgG4 compared to IgG, respectively (Figure 28). Again, the placebo-treated patient
P11 had a equal %HRPost/Pre of 1.02 (orange group), which was consistent with the fact that
this patient sera showed almost no diﬀerence in their amount of sIgG and sIgG4 before and
after immunotherapy. P4 was also a placebo, but showed a slightly %HR reduction with 0.89
(blue group) in %HRPost/Pre corresponding to 11.1 % inhibitionPost/Pre.
When looking at the PS with Post-sera stimulated with rCyp c 1, this system could determine
%HRPost/Pre values for P3 and P12. Interestingly, P12 and P3 had now the lowest %HRPost/Pre
values (green group) with 0.58 (41.9 % inhibition eﬀect) and 0.62 (38.3 % inhibition eﬀect),
respectively.

When taken every performed competitive immunoassay into account, a pattern proposing the
patients having an eﬀect of mCyp c 1 immunotherapy was observed. As seen in Table 10
patient P1, P3, P7, P9, P12, P15, and P16 had the highest chance of successful treatment.

two competitive PS Basophil HR assay performed, 3 out of 14 patients: P1, P7 and P15 were
believed to have the best eﬀect of mCyp c 1 treatment.
