5. DISCUSSION
5
Discussion
5.1
Rabbit Model Systems
The two rabbit model systems; the Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA and the PS Basophil HR assay
were conducted to investigate the inhibitory serological sIgG eﬀect and the inhibitory serological
eﬀect in relation to sIgG/sIgE ratio, respectively.
As the Gad c 1 ELISA was developed and made with serological material from rabbits (TAP
4), it was expected to achieve successful inhibition using TAP 5 and TAP 6 as competitive sub-
stances, since polyclonal rabbit antibodies are able to bind diﬀerent epitopes on parvalbumin,
increasing the chance of inhibition. The results veriﬁed the expectation since it was possible to
obtain 100 % inhibition (using 1% sera in solution), where TAP 5 and TAP 6 in mixture with
cod extract, mopped up all available Gad c 1 (Figure 22). Therefore, using the rabbit as an
animal model to verify the inhibiting properties of IgG, was indeed useful. It could be argued
whether another model system could have been more optimal to use for example goats, chickens
or rodents. Goats are larger animals being able to induce high amounts of antibodies where
antibodies from chickens are easily harvested from the eggs. Rodents have 4 IgG subclasses
matching the same number of human IgG subclasses compared to rabbit, having a single IgG
subclass, namely IgG-κ. However, the rabbit can elicit a strong immune response against for-
eign antigens which is useful for antigens with weak immunogenicity and can produce suﬃcient
high-titer and high-aﬃnity polyclonals, making them highly robust to be used as an animal
model, as validated in our results (Leenaars and Hendriksen, 2005).
Moving from a Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA speciﬁc developed using rabbit anti-Gad c 1 coating
antibodies to a PS Basophil HR immunoassay using human basophils saturated with sIgE from
a ﬁsh allergic individual (1362-57), a diﬀerent response was expected even though using the
same rabbit sera (TAP 6 and NKS). This expectation was based on the fact that the rabbit
antibodies (IgG-κ in 90 % cases) have diﬀerent functionalities compared to human antibodies
(4 IgG subclasses), which could act diﬀerently in human cell suspension under diﬀerent physio-
logical conditions. As seen on Figure 24, the competitive sera samples with TAP 6 were able
to inhibit with 81.7 % at 1:100 sera dilution (1 % sera) and 4.8 % at 1:10000 sera dilution (0.01
% sera) from NKS. This matched the results obtained in Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA when
using NKS as the inhibition reference. Here the inhibition level was a bit lower for samples
with 1 % sera and as well for dilution 0.01%, showing almost no inhibition. Given that a high
inhibition was induced in both immunoassays, was suspected to be due to the polyclonal rabbit
IgG-κ antibodies having a high chance of binding diﬀerent epitopes on Gad c 1. These results
identiﬁed rabbit IgG as useful inhibitory tools in both biochemical and biological immunoassays.
Interestingly, when using the highest rabbit sera dilution of 0.001% in the PS Basophil HR
assay, a reduction in %HR to almost the same level as dilution 0.1% was observed.
66
==PAGE:79==
5. DISCUSSION
This inhibiting trend was inexplicable since, at this dilution, almost no inhibiting substances
were present in the mix with the cod extract, making the cod extract highly dominant. To
resolve whether this trend was a technical error, multiple experiments were conducted (test
trials), but no resolution occurred. One explanation for the trend could be, as described in the
results section, the formation of big cod aggregates inducing either huge allergen-rabbit IgG
immunocomplexes even at a low sera dilution or massive cod aggregates only able to occupy
and crosslink few IgE on basophils, leading to a reduced HR.
Based on theory from the introduction, another explanation for the inhibiting trend could be the
dominant eﬀect of inhibitory receptors that might be present on donor basophils (Scott-Taylor
et al., 2018). When high amounts of Gad c 1 are present, they might bind to rabbit or In-house
sera sIgG loaded FcγRIIB on the basophils and inhibit basophil HR (sIgG not measured for
In-house sera). However, why this trend was opposite for the other low dilution (0.01% sera)
where almost no inhibition occurred (4.8 %) makes this trend open for debate since no obvious
immunological reason can be established.
5.2
Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA (Human Model)
Measurements of Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA was performed with the 14 Pre- and Post-sera to
investigate the inhibitory serological sIgG eﬀect induced by the FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1.
When comparing the qualitative rabbit and human Gad c 1 ELISA models it was observed that
both assays were able to induce a high inhibitory eﬀect in sera dilution 1:100 with around 88 %
inhibition for both TAP 5 and TAP 6 (NKS as inhibition reference) and up to 98 % ODPost/Pre
for P3 followed by P1 (94 %), P13 (60 %), and P15 (83 %). Patients with moderate inhibitory
eﬀect were P2, P5, P7, P9, P16 reaching 10-30 % inhibition, whereas P10 and P12 and the
placebo-treated patients: P4, P6, and P11 acted as placebos having inhibitory eﬀects of (-)3-2.4
%.
The highly successful performance of the Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA using human sera was
unquestionable. These high inhibitory results obtained, especially from P1 (94 %) and P3 (98
%) containing 1 % sera mixed cod extract, implies that sIgG had mopped up all free available
Gad c 1. This high inhibition might indicate that both low and high aﬃne sIgG antibodies bind
Gad c 1 due to the high concentration of sIgG antibodies present in the wells. Importantly,
these high inhibition results were similar to ﬁndings found by Freidl et al. (2017). In this study,
rabbit anti-mCyp c 1 was used to inhibit the binding of ﬁsh allergic patients IgE to ELISA plate
bound rCyp c 1. Similar to our results, a full inhibition was almost obtained using a human
sera dilution of 1%.
Since only a moderate inhibition percent (10-30 %) were observed for some of the patients (P2,
P5, P7, P9, and P16) when conducting Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA seems reasonable since
biological and serological variance exists. This variance can be observed when analyzing the
induction of sIgE, sIgG and sIgG4 antibodies before and after mCyp c 1 treatment, where no
indicative pattern was observed for these patients, all having diﬀerent antibody ratios.
67
==PAGE:80==
5. DISCUSSION
When analyzing the results for P10 and P12 which had high ODPost/Pre values and which matched
the placebo-treated patients, the result for P12 seemed true since no diﬀerence in sIgG or sIgG4
was observed before and after mCyp c 1 immunotherapy. Opposite did P10 induce a high sIgG/
sIgG4 diﬀerence between Pre and Post-sera which did not correlate with the ODPost/Pre results.
One reason for this could be a low aﬃnity of the IgG antibodies towards Gad c1, making them
unable to bind and thus inhibit the HR. Another possibility could be the equal induction of
sIgE before and after treatment for P10, making sIgE dominant in the setup.
Another aspect in the Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA measurements using human sera is the
eﬀect of "invisible" antibodies, i.e. non-IgG/non-IgE antibodies react with non-allergenic com-
ponents in the cod extract. The qualitative measurements in Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA do
not discriminate between inhibition induced by sIgG or sIgE antibodies and also do not dis-
criminate between the non- or speciﬁc antibodies responding to non-allergenic components and
allergens. This might hamper interpretation of the results, as veriﬁed by Aalberse et al. (2001),
since false-positive results would be generated if non-IgG/non-IgE antibodies bind to the cod
extract before reaching anti-Gad c 1 in the wells. Even if pure Gad c 1 was used instead of cod
extract for the measurement of speciﬁc IgG antibodies, it is not possible to distinguish with
certainty between allergen-speciﬁc IgG/IgE antibodies inducing the blocking eﬀect (Flicker and
Valenta, 2003).
Instead of developing a new optimized ELISA to reveal the inhibitory eﬀect related to the
sIgG/sIgG4 serological proﬁle in humans, a comparison of the Gad c 1 ELISA results with Im-
munoCAP measurements could be evaluated. In view of the well-performed Competitive Gad c
1 ELISA using human sera from the FAST study, it was expected to achieve a high mutual re-
lationship between the two assays; quantitative ImmunoCAP and qualitative Competitive Gad
c 1 ELISA. These assays were both raised against Gad c 1 and designed as a sandwich assay
with a solid phase, where allergen-antibody interactions occur. The results demonstrated how
a moderate signiﬁcant relationship with a rs of -0.65 when comparing ELISA ODPost/Pre with
sIgG4Post/Pre, and a weak insigniﬁcant association (rs -0.38) when comparing with sIgGPost/Pre
were observed, which were not as expected. It could be argued that the two procedures are very
diﬀerent even though both assays are biochemically. ImmunoCAP measurements give informa-
tion about the balance of power of sIgG/sIgG4 but do not take the binding quality into account.
When the allergen density in ImmunoCAP is suﬃciently high the sIgG/sIgG4 even at relatively
low aﬃnity will be detectable as described by Aalberse et al. (2001). Whereas the Competitive
Gad c 1 ELISA gives a more immunological relevant picture of the immunological response,
especially when including the competitive substances where the binding quality could play a
bigger role. Besides the diﬀerent advantages and disadvantages of both methods, considering
the two performances of ELISA and ImmunoCAP helped strengthen the suspicion about which
patients could have an eﬀect of the FAST vaccine. The correlation plots (Figure 27) showed
clearly how P1, P3, P13, and P15 could have a high immunological eﬀect of the vaccine.
68
==PAGE:81==
5. DISCUSSION
5.3
PS Basophil HR with Pre- and Post-sera
When screening all the patients according to their CAP classes for their ability to passively
sensitize and mediate a cod extract or rCyp c 1-induced HR-response, it was, in general, ob-
served that an increase in reactivity for both allergens matched the increase in CAP classes
(subsubsection 4.1.3), having sIgE levels >3.6 ng/mL that enabled a positive HR-response.
These ﬁndings correspond with the results obtained by Stoﬀersen (2012), where patients having
a higher CAP class than 1 (1 kUA/L = 2.4 ng/mL) were able to mediate an HR-response upon
allergen stimulation. These ﬁndings indicated that having a reduced amount of sIgE, resulted
in a reduced amount of crosslinking events during allergen challenge, leading to an HR under
cut-oﬀlevel. Contradicting these ﬁndings, it was observed that some patients (PS w. Pre-sera:
P6 and P16, PS w. Post-sera: P6, P7, and P13) had reduced HR reactivity when performing
PS even though belonging to CAP class 3. According to theory, these patients should be able to
mediate a moderate response due to their level of sIgE but did not. These observations change
the picture since having a high amount of sIgE, does not necessarily correlate with the ability
to mediate eﬀector cell degranulation in the presence of an allergen. Here aﬃnity might play a
role as well. Studies have shown that individual sIgEs have a broad range of aﬃnities towards
natural isoforms of allergens (Christensen et al., 2008, 2010). Thus having an IgE repertoire of
high clonality, but with low aﬃnity might result in low binding properties. Opposite, would a
single IgE antibody of high aﬃnity be enough for the crosslinking to another IgE antibody, into
an allergen-sIgE binding complex (Aalberse et al., 2001; Christensen et al., 2008), resulting in
a high HR-response.
Another observation achieved by Stoﬀersen (2012) was an increase in sensitivity with increasing
CAP classes, like the reactivity increases with increasing CAP classes. This trend was also ob-
served in our results, where patient sera with high sIgE level were more sensitive than those with
low sIgE level, however independently of which CAP class the individual patient belonged to.
The fact that diﬀerences in sensitivity among patients were observed reﬂect that aﬃnity might
play a role in allergic responses since more aﬃne sera (for those with high sIgE) would induce
a high HR-response at a low allergen concentration. This scenario was veriﬁed by Christensen
et al. (2008), showing a positive relationship between IgE aﬃnity and basophil activation.
Another observation that could be related to aﬃnity was the shift in CAP class for three sera
(P3, P10, and P11) using PS with Post-sera. P3 who was able to induce more sIgE after the
treatment compared to before, resulted in a feasible PS using Post-sera. But when using P3 in
the Competitive PS Basophil HR, the response did not reach cut-oﬀ. This implies that even
though a higher induction of sIgE was observed, the sIgE level was not able to generate as high
allergen response as those patients having both a high sIgE level before and after the treatment.
This trend was supported by multiple studies, verifying a clear increase in sIgE without clinical
and functional relevance (Shamji et al., 2017). Opposite P3 did P10 and P11 induce lower sIgE
levels after treatment. These new levels did not seem to aﬀect the results since they were able
to mediate an HR-response as before treatment.
69
==PAGE:82==
5. DISCUSSION
This made P10 and P11 feasible both in PS Basophil HR and Competitive PS Basophil HR.
These results might indicate that the sIgE antibodies retain their aﬃnity even after an induction
or a reduction occurs.
5.4
Competitive PS Basophil HR - Pre- vs. Post-sera
In this thesis, we have evaluated the immunological changes that occur in response to mCyp c
1 immunotherapy to observe whether a shift in sIgE/IgG (sIgG4) balance indeed occurs. This
was evaluated by performing PS Basophil HR assays using sera from before and after mCyp c
1 immunotherapy from 14 codﬁsh allergic patients.
5.4.1
Assay Inﬂuence
When evaluating our results at a systemic plan comparing PS with Pre- or Post-sera as two
diﬀerent systems, it was acknowledged that the two systems showed diﬀerent trends. As stated
earlier, when designing PS with Post-sera a more complex system was developed, believed to
have less and/or low aﬃne sIgE antibodies bound to the basophil surface compared to PS with
Pre-sera having multiple and/or high aﬃne sIgE loaded on the surface. This combined with
the fact that not necessarily all sIgG or sIgE would be bound to the basophils after PS, thus
be present in the cell suspension surroundings, and therefore also would be able to bind to the
Pre- or Post-sera+allergen samples as well, increase the inhibition even further. These scenarios
might explain the smaller HR ratio observed between Pre+allergen and Post+allergen using PS
with Post-sera compared to the PS with Pre-sera as seen in Figure 37.
Another suspicion for the diﬀerence between the assays could be the use of diﬀerent blood
donors. However, the best circumstances were actually applied when performing PS with Post-
sera since a super donor was used making the system more sensitive and thus favor the chance
to detect a low %HRPost/Pre, compared to PS with Pre-sera where an optimal donor with a lower
PMA/ionomycin level was applied. Even though trying to keep the basophil donor a constant
factor in the assays (by calculating %HR), other factors such as diﬀerences in receptors expressed
on the basophil surface could inﬂuence the results, inhibiting or activating the basophils in a
higher or lower degree dependent on the donor selected.
The diﬀerence in basophil donor selection could also be one of the reasons why diﬀerent patients
were applied in the two competitive setups (Competitive PS Basophil HR with Pre-sera or Post-
sera). The use of diﬀerent patients in the two setups blur the picture for which patients that
might have an eﬀect of the treatment, which renders one of the main drawbacks when applying
Competitive PS Basophil HR for AIT evaluation.
Using basophils to evaluate the eﬀect of AIT, has, as stated, its limitations besides having
basophils which are viable, fragile to handle and have a short lifespan. This had also been
veriﬁed by other AIT studies (Varricchi et al., 2018; Shamji et al., 2017) highlighting the need
for more standardized methods when applying basophils in immunoassays.
70
==PAGE:83==
5. DISCUSSION
5.4.2
Immunological Inﬂuence
After performing PS Basophil HR immunoassays with both Pre- and Post-sera, it was acknowl-
edged that a correlation between the induction of sIgG as well as sIgG4 and the suppression of
basophil HR indeed occurred. When looking at the ImmunoCAP measurements, all patients
showed an increase in the ratio for both sIgG and sIgG4 after mCyp c 1 immunotherapy, un-
like those patients treated with placebo (P4, P6, and P11). Interestingly, a diﬀerence in the
number of IgG antibodies produced was diﬀerent for each patient, some patient inducing more
or less sIgG than sIgG4 after treatment. Even though elevated serum concentrations of sIgG4
has been demonstrated to be the main predictive biomarker for AIT success, as concluded in
EAACI position paper: Shamji et al. (2017), it is clear from our results using PS with Pre-sera
that inducing a high sIgG or/and IgG4 level both resulted in a suppressed HR. This evaluation
was based on P12 and P16 having the highest sIgGPost/Pre and P1 and P7 having the highest
sIgG4Post/Pre as well as P15 having both moderate sIgGPost/Pre and sIgG4Post/Pre all had the abil-
ity to inhibit basophil HR (Table 8). The fact that both sIgG and sIgG4 play a role in allergy
resolution seems logic since they tailor diﬀerent parts of the allergic response. sIgG which are
predominately produced at the ﬁrst allergen exposure in large quantities and which are able
to activate the complement system, whereas inhibitory sIgG4 potently binds to allergens and
have regulatory purposes on basophils, depriving sIgE before triggering an allergic response
(Figure 6) (Scott-Taylor et al., 2018).
When evaluating the correlation between PS Basophil HR with Pre-sera %HRPost/Pre and
sIgGPost/Pre or sIgG4Post/Pre, it is clear that even though both sIgG and sIgG4 seems to have a
synergistic eﬀect when looking at some of the individual patients, the trend was changed when
including all patients in the evaluation. Here a better correlation between sIgG4Post/Pre and
%HRPost/Pre was observed, having a signiﬁcant association and a higher correlation coeﬃcient
than with sIgGPost/Pre. As described in the results section, it was observed that patients (P1,
P7, P12, P15 and P16) inducing a high sIgG4Post/Pre level towards codﬁsh were able to suppress
the HR in a higher degree than those inducing a limited amount of sIgG4 (P2, P4, P5, P10 and
P11). Interestingly was P12 able to generate a low %HRPost/Pre even though inducing an equal
amount of sIgG and sIgG4 antibodies towards Gad c 1 before and after treatment (Figure 25),
indicating that sIgG antibodies towards other allergens in the cod extract than Gad c 1 are
generated which are able to suppress the HR.
The same trend was observed in regards to sIgG4Post/Pre when performing PS Basophil HR with
Post-sera, where an even stronger signiﬁcant correlation between sIgG4Post/Pre and %HRPost/Pre
was observed than for PS Basophil HR performed with Pre-sera. For PS with Post-sera, P12 was
now excluded and P16 showed a high %HRPost/Pre which was diﬀerent from PS with Pre-sera.
Instead did P9, which was excluded in PS with Pre-sera, generates a low %HRPost/Pre, which
matched its high sIgG and sIgG4Post/Pre ratio. In regards to the correlation between sIgGPost/Pre
and %HRPost/Pre no signiﬁcant correlation was observed when performing PS Basophil HR with
Post-sera, indicating no synergistic eﬀect between the two antibodies.
71
==PAGE:84==
5. DISCUSSION
These ﬁndings were supported by multiple food AIT studies, identifying sIgG4 as the main
player in the resolution of allergy (Burks et al., 2012; Vickery et al., 2013; Santos et al., 2015;
Shamji et al., 2012).
If taken the induction of sIgE antibodies into account, it is clear that a more skewed picture
is detected, where approximately 50 % of the patients (P1, P2, P3, P9, P12, P13 and P16)
induced more sIgE after than before mCyp c 1 treatment. A reason for this induction of sIgE
after AIT could be explained by the short AIT duration. It has been shown that sIgE levels
initially are increased after AIT (might be due to other natural allergen exposure) and only
decreased over several years (>3 years) of AIT (Shamji et al., 2017).
One could speculate
whether the induction would aﬀect the results by outweighing the inhibitory sIgG eﬀect, but
this seemed not to be the case since the patients (included in the setup) inducing the highest
level of sIgE (P1, P12, P16) also generated the highest %HRPost/Pre ratio. This indicates that
sIgE work submissive compared to sIgG and sIgG4 antibodies. These results are supported by
Shamji et al. (2017) illustrating no clinical outcomes linked to an elevated level of sIgE during
AIT since TH2A (allergy-inducing cells) promote sIgE production (Wambre et al., 2017) and
early- and late responses in the skin are reduced.
As clearly stated above, a signiﬁcant correlation is highly observed between measured sIgG4Post/Pre
and %HRPost/Pre for almost all patients. However, three patients: P2, P5, and P10 can be dis-
tinguished from the rest in both PS Basophil HR with Pre- and Post-sera. As seen in Figure 28
all the tree patients are able to generate moderate to high levels of sIgG and sIgG4 after the
treatment and therefore would have been expected to induce a lower %HRPost/Pre than the
placebo-treated patients. However, this trend was not observed when performing PS Basophil
HR, having ratios near or above 1 (Table 8 and Table 9), placing them close to the placebos
(the same trend was observed for P10 in Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA). These results might
indicate that the IgG antibodies in the Post-sera from these patients might not be as aﬃne,
making them unable to mediate a response diﬀerent from before treatment. If only evaluating
which patients that would have an eﬀect of mCyp c 1 treatment by ImmunoCAP measurements,
these patients would have been included, but would properly not have the highest immunolog-
ical. This highlights the importance of including a biological assay to increase the chance of a
successful AIT.
To sum up, on the results from PS Basophil HR and the ImmunoCAP, it was expected that the
patients that have the highest chance of mCyp c 1 AIT eﬀect would be the patients generating
the highest diﬀerence between their Pre- and Post-sera. Out of the 14 patients evaluated, 6
active-treated patients (P1, P7, P9, P12, P15, and P16) were believed to have a detectable
eﬀect of mCyp c 1 immunotherapy (Table 10), having %HRPost/Pre of ≤0.64 corresponding
to a ≥36% HR-reduction. Interestingly, these patients both belonged to group 1 (P1 and P7)
and group 2 (P9, P12, P15 and P16), receiving diﬀerent mCyp c 1 doses (subsection 3.1),
indicating that a small dose of mCyp c 1 is enough to detect a diﬀerence after AIT. Since not
all patients were aﬀected by the treatment, veriﬁed that allergy is highly polymorphic and that
AIT, therefore, is highly diverse in individual patients (Jönsson and Daëron, 2012).
72
==PAGE:85==
5. DISCUSSION
5.4.3
Allergen Inﬂuence - Cod Extract vs. rCyp c 1
In all PS Basophil HR immunoassays, except the assays with rabbit sera and the test trials with
human sera, the cod extract and the puriﬁed rCyp c 1 were used to stimulate the basophils.
When performing PS with both Pre- and Post-sera, the basophil reactivity when stimulating
with both cod extract and rCyp c1 was almost identical (subsubsection 4.1.3) indicating that
both allergens are able to activate basophils in a similar way and release equal amounts of his-
tamine. Though, when moving to the Competitive PS Basophil HR immunoassays, a diﬀerent
pattern was observed, showing a reduced %HRPost/Pre when using rCyp c 1 as stimulant com-
pared to the cod extract.
As stated in the results section, this was not expected. This argument was based on the fact
that Gad c 1 and carp rCyp c 1 shares high homologous (68%) and shares epitope binding sites
(Figure 3). Indeed it was expected that rCyp c 1 would generate a higher HR compared to the
cod extract since rCyp c 1 has the highest ability for crosslinking FcϵRI, since it contains most
of the IgE conformational epitopes from various ﬁsh species (70% epitopes in allergen extracts
from cod, tuna, and salmon) (Swoboda et al., 2002). One sensible reason for rCyp c 1 not being
able to generate as high %HRPost/Pre as the cod extract when performing PS Basophil HR using
Pre-sera, could be explained by the low amount of sIgE antibodies towards rCyp c 1 present in
the Pre-sera compared to the sIgE raised against cod extract. It could be speculated whether
this low amount of sIgE towards rCyp c 1 present on the basophils, would generate a reduced
response due to limited crosslinking when stimulating with rCyp c 1. Opposite, would a high
response be observed when challenging with cod extract, due to a higher load of receptors di-
rected towards cod, since the patients are codﬁsh allergic. When evaluating the PS Basophil HR
with Post-sera, a little higher %HRPost/Pre was observed when using rCyp c 1 compared to PS
Basophil HR with Pre-sera. This higher ratio could be explained by Post-sera being more prone
to respond to rCyp c 1. Going from a serological proﬁle with almost no sIgG and sIgE levels
against rCyp c 1 to probably have developed some with crucial speciﬁcities in the Post-sera,
would increase the ratio. Upon the challenge with rCyp c 1 in the PS system with Post-sera,
the basophils and their newly developed high-aﬃnity sIgE might have been more sensitive to
react to rCyp c 1, thus release more histamine compared to the PS system with Pre-sera.
Furthermore, when analyzing PS with Pre-sera and Post-sera and their correlation with the
values obtained from rCyp %HRPost/Pre and cod extract, PS with Post-sera demonstrated a
strong association (rs 0.70) compared to PS with Pre-sera having a moderate relationship (rs
0.42). This variation in correlation results can again be because of a more prone system in PS
with Post-sera having better sensitivity towards rCyp c 1.
Another reason for the diﬀerence in rCyp c 1 %HRPost/Pre and cod extract %HRPost/Pre stimu-
lation could also be due to donor variation (optimal vs. super donor) as stated earlier.
73
==PAGE:86==
5. DISCUSSION
5.5
Biochemical and Biological Immunoassays
After performing the Competitive PS Basophil HR assays, we were able to verify the proposed
mechanism behind AIT in regards to a suppressed HR during challenging with allergens after
mCyp c 1 treatment. Therefore, the idea of PS Basophil HR immunoassay being used as a
measurable indicator for validation of the eﬃcacious in FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 is highly possible,
especially since the PS Basophil HR is depended on whether the induced IgG antibodies have
high enough aﬃnity to inhibit the basophil response, which are not possible when using bio-
chemical immunoassays. On the other hand, it should be acknowledged that a high correlation
between the two methods are obviously and the sIgG and sIgG4 measurements detected by
ImmunoCAP are indeed worth to notice when evaluating AIT.
One thing is the elevated level of sIgG/sIgG4 induced after AIT, which inhibits basophil HR,
another thing is whether the immunological response is high enough to make any clinical dif-
ference in the patients life. As stated by multiple studies (Flicker and Valenta, 2003; Shamji
et al., 2012; James et al., 2011; Shamji et al., 2017), no functional outcome in form of symptoms
and medication score have been observed after food AIT. This has as well been concluded after
analyzing the result obtained in SPT challenged with ﬁsh in the active treatment compared to
placebo in the FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 phaseIIb trial. The fact that no diﬀerence between placebo
and mCyp c 1 treatment have been observed when performing SPT contradicts our results,
where a clear diﬀerence between placebo-treated patients (P4, P6, P11) and mCyp c 1 treated
patient was observed; P4, P6, and P11 being unable to release histamine upon allergen stimula-
tion in all setups. This did also correlate with their serum levels of sIgG, sIgG4 and sIgE, which
was not changed before and after immunotherapy. This diﬀerence in results might be due to the
two diﬀerent cell types activated, which respond diﬀerently in each set-up; mast cells activated
in the skin by SPT and basophils isolated from the blood in Competitive PS Basophil HR.
To validate whether mCyp c 1 immunotherapy had worked, especially for P1, P3, P9, P12, P15
and P16 a DBPCFC with ﬁsh and/or a questionnaire given to the patients would have been
ideal. In this way, a more true evaluation of ﬁsh allergen immunotherapy would be given.
5.6
Related to the FAST Study
The FAST phaseIIa study was conducted as a proof of concept for the safety and pharmacody-
namics of sIgG(sIgG4)/sIgE of the mCyp c 1 treatment (Malling, 2013). The serological samples
from the study were analyzed and obtained before and after 4 months of mCyp c 1 vaccina-
tion. It could be speculated whether a more solid diﬀerence between Pre- and Post-sera could
have been achieved in PS Basophil HR if the AIT was conducted in a larger timeframe than 4
months. The article by Shamji and Durham (2017) illustrates how the level of sIgG/sIgG4 is
in its exponential phase after 4 months of immunotherapy and that a plateau is ﬁrst achieved
after around 8 months of duration. Thus, increasing the time frame with additional 4 months
might have induced a higher blocking eﬀect of the Post-sera containing sIgG/sIgG4.
74
==PAGE:87==
5. DISCUSSION
The fact that the patients sIgE levels were initially increased after 4 months of mCyp c 1
treatment in 50 % of the cases, was consistent with other AIT studies (Shamji et al., 2017).
The reason for the induction of sIgE could be due to similar events of the short-lived IgE
plasma cells responses observed in murine models by Freidl et al. (2017) (Wu and Scheerens,
2014). Here, the increase of sIgE level might lead to false-positive results in the SPT, since only
long-term studies have shown that a gradual decrease in sIgE levels occur over several years of
SCIT (Shamji et al., 2017). Therefore evaluating the sIgE levels cannot be managed in short
time frames such as in phaseIIa studies.
In general, food AIT studies including the FAST ﬁsh study lack under diﬀerent conditions such
as ; limited study populations, lack of diversity in study groups, high variability of study design
(sample size, maintenance dose, duration length), the economic aspect with lack of economic
impact data, the lack of immunologic biomarkers that correlate with clinical outcomes, and the
lack of comparative eﬃcacy studies of the diﬀerent food AIT forms (Burks et al., 2018). In
relation to the FAST study, it especially lacks under economic feasibility, a small study group
(15 patients in phaseIIa), and a short clinical duration in the phaseIIa study.
75
==PAGE:88==
6. CONCLUSION
6
Conclusion
By developing and performing Competitive PS Basophil HR immunoassays using sera from 14
ﬁsh allergic patients before and after retrieving mCyp c 1 immunotherapy we have been able
to evaluate PS Basophil HR as a measurable indicator for successful ﬁsh allergen speciﬁc im-
munotherapy (AIT). Indeed, by comparing the %HR from before and after mCyp c 1 treatment,
a reduction in the HR from the basophil when stimulating with the cod extract was clearly ob-
served, especially for patients inducing high levels of inhibitory sIgG4 antibodies measured by
the ImmunoCAP® system.
This trend was also observed when performing Competitive Gad c 1 ELISA, where a reduction in
OD-values signiﬁcantly correlated with the induction of sIgG4 after mCyp c 1 immunotherapy.
When taken all performed Competitive immunoassays into account, 6 active-treated patients
out of 14 patients (including 3 placebos) were believed to have beneﬁted from the mCyp c 1
treatment. In the biological Competitive immunoassays, this eﬀect was expressed by a low
%HRPost/Pre of ≤0.64 corresponding to a ≥36% HR-reduction after mCyp c 1 treatment. No-
ticeably, only a weak insigniﬁcant association was observed when correlating the %HRPost/Pre
with IgGPost/Pre, indicating IgG4 being the major player in the resolution of allergy. However
more experiments showing identical results are required to provide suﬃcient power of the study
and to ﬁnally evaluate the immunological mechanism behind and IgG4 involvement in allergy
resolution.
Given high correlations between results from PS Basophil HR immunoassays and ImmunoCAP®
measurements were observed, identiﬁes the biochemical ImmunoCAP® system as a highly pre-
dictive tool to evaluate the eﬀect of AIT. However using the ImmunoCAP® system together
with PS Basophil HR would properly give an even better evaluation of AIT, since PS Basophil
HR is dependent on receptor aﬃnity and avidity which cannot be revealed by the ImmunoCAP®
system.
In conclusion, we can verify our hypothesis that sIgG and especially sIgG4 induced by FAST
mCyp c 1.0101 competes with sIgE for β-parvalbumin binding leading to reduced HR in patients
with ﬁsh allergy.
76
==PAGE:89==
7. PERSPECTIVES FOR FURTHER RESEARCH
7
Perspectives for Further Research
In this thesis, we investigated the ability of Competitive PS Basophil HR to evaluate the eﬀect
of FAST ﬁsh mCyp c 1 immunotherapy. Performing PS Basophil HR requires highly skilled spe-
cialists and fresh optimal buﬀy coat donors which are needed for every conducted experiment,
this makes the procedure often time-consuming and laborious. Therefore, more experiments are
needed to be reproduced to verify the results and same tendencies are needed to ﬁnally conclude
whether PS Basophil HR can be used in further evaluation on AIT. As stated in the discussion,
the studies symptom and rescue medication scores could subsequently have been conducted by
DBPCFC with ﬁshes to further validate if these ﬁndings in PS Basophil HR actually correlates
with the clinical outcome.
During PS basophil HR and the competitive PS basophil HR, some patients were excluded
because the HistaReader quantiﬁed the ﬁsh allergic patients in the area below the cut-oﬀ: 10
ng/mL. In further research, it could be interestingly to ﬁnd other more sensitive systems for
measuring HR, which could measure down to 1 ng/mL or even lower so no patient sera should
be excluded from the experiments. Another approach for measuring basophil degranulation is
by the BAT, a single-cell analyze method. BAT has a high sensitivity and has been able to
measure allergic patients even with a low basophil number in the setup (Larsen et al., 2017).
Thus using the BAT analyzing Pre- and Post-sera for determination of factors in serum could be
used and developed as a second test to conﬁrm the ﬁndings in the Competitive PS Basophil HR
immunoassay. Developing a BAT with intracellular staining of Phycoerythrin (PE)–conjugated
diamine oxidase (DAO), could be compared with the obtained results (Nullens et al., 2013).
Another validated and highly reproducible ﬂow-cytometry based method such as the IgE-
Facilitated Allergen Binding (IgE-FAB) assay using serological samples, can be assessed for
evaluating AIT. IgE-FAB is developed speciﬁcally for evaluating on the sIgG4 inhibitory eﬀect
on IgE-facilitated allergen presentation and the stimulation of basophil HR. In some studies, the
IgE-FAB has been reported to correlate with clinical outcome, though only a limited amount
of studies exists and the instrument for measuring IgE-FAB is not available anymore. EAACI
suggests that this method is evaluated in further studies to ﬁnd predictable biomarkers in AIT.
(Shamji et al., 2017).
For a deeper understanding of the eﬀect of AIT, mast cells are very essential for allergy and its
resolution. The focus in further research could be on the biological diﬀerences between mast
cells and basophils, which serological factors play a crucial role in AIT with focus on aﬃnity and
clonality. As described in the introduction, the mast cells do have poorly expression of FcγRIIB
and this must be investigated if this limits the inhibitory role of IgG4 on mast cells. Besides
SPT as an indicator of skin mast cell activation, other studies on mast cells can be assessed
by mucosal biopsies and analyzed with immunohistochemistry to examine the functionality or
assessed by ex vivo microdialysis used for preclinical assessment and in situ microdialysis to
study the pharmacological eﬀect on dermal mast-cell HR from before and after immunotherapy
(Baumann and Skov, 2017).
77

L. Zuidmeer-Jongejan, M. Fernandez-Rivas, L. K. Poulsen, A. Neubauer, J. Asturias, L. Blom, J. Boye,
C. Bindslev-Jensen, M. Clausen, R. Ferrara, et al. Fast: towards safe and eﬀective subcutaneous immunother-
apy of persistent life-threatening food allergies. Clinical and translational allergy, 2(1):5, 2012.
L. Zuidmeer-Jongejan, H. Huber, I. Swoboda, N. Rigby, S. A. Versteeg, B. M. Jensen, S. Quaak, J. H. Akkerdaas,
L. Blom, J. Asturias, et al.
Development of a hypoallergenic recombinant parvalbumin for ﬁrst-in-man
subcutaneous immunotherapy of ﬁsh allergy. International archives of allergy and immunology, 166(1):41–51,
2015.
84
==PAGE:97==
Tracking Information
Start Date
August 2013
Completion Date
October 2014 (Final data collection date for primary outcome measure)
Primary Outcome
Safety in the form of number and severity of adverse events
Safety is evaluated by number and severity of adverse events
Secondary Outcome
Speciﬁc IgE: To study the pharmaco-dynamics of the mCyp.
Speciﬁc IgE. IgG4: Immunologic parameter.
Skin Prick Test: Pharmaco-dynamics of the mCyp
Descriptive Information
Oﬃcial Title
FAST-Fish -Food Allergy Speciﬁc Treatment for Fish Allergy.
Study Design
Allocation: Randomized Intervention
Model: Parallel Assignment
Masking: Double (Participant, Investigator)
Intervention
Biological: mCyp c 12 patient groups with diﬀerent doses of allergen.
Other Name: A modiﬁed hypo-allergenic Parvalbumin
Study Arms
Experimental: group 1
5 patients (P1, P2, P3, P5, P7) received 10 single rising doses of mCyp c 1
from 0.6 ng to 6µg and 2 maintenance doses, and 2 patients (P4 and P6) received placebo.
Experimental: Group 2
6 patients (P9, P10, P12, P13, P15, P16) received 10 single rising doses of mCyp c 1
from 6 ng to 60µg and 2 maintenance doses, and 2 patients (P11 and P14) received placebo.
Recruitment Information
Enrollment
15 human patients
Inclusion Criteria
- Male or female subject from 18 to 65 years old and in general good health as
determined by past medical history and physical examination.
- Case history of allergy to ﬁsh ingestion.
- Speciﬁc IgE to ﬁsh by either a positive SPT to cod ﬁsh extract or an ImmunoCAP to
cod ﬁsh above 0.70 kUA/L,(Class 2) at screening.
- Positive DBPCFC with ﬁsh within the last 2 years.
- FEV1 (lung capacity) at least 80% of predicted values at screening.
- Subject accepting to comply fully with the protocol.
- Woman of child bearing potential: a negative urine pregnancy test at screening visit,
subject must receive a medically eﬀective contraceptive method during the study
Exclusion Criteria
- Food Anaphylactic Reaction: anaphylactic shock due to ﬁsh intake.
- Speciﬁc IgE (ImmunoCAP) to ﬁsh parvalbumin (rCyp c 1) below 0.35 kUA/L
Ongoing pollen Immunotherapy (SIT).
- Any clinical condition that contraindicates SIT (EAACI-guidelines).
- Any signiﬁcant clinical condition that the investigators judged might hamper
the patient’s safety or the study outcomes, these diseases include, but are not limited to,
cardiovascular disease, malignancy, hepatic disease, renal disease,
haematological disease, neurological disease, immunological and endocrine disease.
- Ongoing treatment with betablockers or ACE-inhibitors.
- Impossibility for the patient to comply with the scheduled visits.
- Pregnancy or nursing.
- Uncontrolled asthma. Subject participated in a clinical trial within 3 mo. prior to this one.
- Subject with a history of drug or alcohol abuse.
- Investigators, co-investigators, their children or spouses and all the collaborators
should not be enrolled in the study. Patients with concurrent allergy symptoms
can be included if they manage without antihistamines during screening and treatments.
Sex/Gender/Ages
Sexes Eligible for Study: All, 18 Years to 65 Years (Adult)
Administrative Information
NCT Number
NCT02017626
Study Sponsor
Rigshospitalet, Denmark
Collaborators
University Hospital, Gentofte, Copenhagen Odense University Hospital
Investigators
Hans-Joergen Malling, MD Allergy Clinic, Gentofte University Hospital

B. APPENDIX: ALLERGEN SEQUENCES AND ALIGNMENT
B
Appendix: Allergen Sequences and Alignment
Procedure: The deduced amino acid sequences of rCyp c 1.0101 (UniProt Q8UUS3) were aligned with mCyp
c 1 (FASTA modiﬁed by authors), Gad c 1.0101 (UniProt P02622, M inserted in N-terminal) and Gad m 1.0202
(UniProt Q90YK9) in T-Coﬀee multiple sequence alignment program (EMBL-EBI). rCyp c 1.0101 are modiﬁed
to mCyp c 1.0101 by substituting the ﬁrst and third aspartic acid (D) of the Ca2+ binding sites (CD and
EF) to nonpolar alanine (A) residues at position (highlighted in red): D52A, D54A, D91A, and D93A. The
sequences was copied to LaTex and sequence alignment created by authors in LaTex with TexShade package.
Color interpretation : White = non conserved, Magenta = similar, Blue = ≥50% conserved, and Purple =
≥80 % conserved. UniProt codes: Chicken (Avian, P19753), Clu_h1 (Herring, C6GKU6), Cyp_c1 (Carp,
Q8UUS3), Frog_edible (amphiphan, P02617), Gad_c1 (Baltic Cod, P02622), Gad_m1 (Atlantic Cod, Q90YK9
(ﬁsh from Bergen)), Human (mammalian, P0CE72), Onc_m1 (Rainbow Trout, E0WDA4), Sal_s1 (Salmon,
Q91482), Sco_s1 (Mackerel, D3GME4), Thu_a1 (Tuna, E0WDA4).
4
==PAGE:101==

1. Screening of buffy coat - selection and storage

Principle: 
In this procedure, donor basophils are identified in the screening. The selection is based on 
their responsiveness and native allergenic profile.

Procedure: 
1. Screening of buffy coat - selection and storage. 
Fresh buffy coat blood is screened for aIgE responsiveness, responsiveness to any relevant 
allergen and maximal histamine release (PMA/Ionomycin). Highly aIgE responding donor with 
no allergic profile, low background and high maximal histamine release is preferably selected.    
 
Cell stimulation (per donor) 
1. Mix 1 mL buffy coat blood (remaining blood stores as 8°C) with 9 mL pipes buffer 
(pipes removes remaining plasma proteins) = washed blood. Centrifuge for 10 min at 
600 xg , RT (Accel/Deccel: 5/3). Remove the supernatant - avoid disturbing the white 
cell layer - and add pipes buffer to a total volume of 3 mL (25µl x 100 wells =2.5 mL ). 
 
2. Add 25 µL pipes buffer to screenings plate (if used). 
 
3. Add 25 μL pipes buffer to standard (column 1)/blank-wells (row 1 and 2) on HI plate 
and dilutions of aIgE, allergen (extract) or solution for maximal HR (PMA/Ionomycin) to 
wells. See supplement for dilution examples  
 
4. Add 25 μL diluted buffy coat blood to all wells. 
 
5. Put a lid on the plates and incubate them for 30 min at 37°C. During incubation, 
released histamine will bind to the glass fibers.  
 
The calibration plate, doing following: 
- 50µl pipes buffer 
- 30 min incubation at 37°C 
- Wash with demineralised water 5 times 
- 75µl OPA for 10 min.  
- 75µl pherchloric acid 0.59% to stop the colormetric development 
- Ready for HR reading/calibration 
 
 
Big glass tubes 
==PAGE:115==
SOP name: 
 
SOP no.: 
p. 4   
 
 
 
This document is printed 14. august 2018 
 
Quantification of released histamine 
 
3. 
Wash plates Wash plates 5x with demineralised water starting with column 1.  
Dry plates by slapping them repeatedly onto thick layers of absorbing paper.  (You can 
stop here and leave the plates up-side-down in the draw, until analysis). 
  
4. 
Add 150 μL SDS Solution 0,4% and incubate plates for 10 min at 37°C. 
5. 
Wash plates manually with demineralised water (5x2 both ways to make sure that the 
SDS is removed completely), dry plates.   
 
6. 
Add 75 μL OPA Solution to all wells – remember to start the timer at the first 
plate/first well. OPA react with the primary amines in histamine within the glass fibers 
 
7. 
After 10 min, stop the reaction by adding 75 µL perchloric acid 0,59 %.  
 
 
Allow the reaction to occur for a few minutes and read the plates on HistaReader.  
 
Storage of blood 
When a optimal donor has been identified, the buffy coat is added diluted Recombinant 
Human IL-3 to a final concentration of 10 pg/mL (add X μL of IL-3 corresponding to X mL of 
buffy coat, eg. 40 mL buffy coat is added 40 μL Diluted Recombinant Human IL-3) and stored 
overnight at 4°C. The blood can be stored for two day.

Dilutions:  
Cod extracts (Cod 1)  
100mg powder /ml = 100.000µg/ml 
To reach a start concentration of 100µg/ml, a dilution to 1:1000 (100.000/100µg/ml) is 
performed: 
• 1:10  100µl extract + 900 µl Pipes  
• 1:100  10µl + 990µl Pipes = 1000µl

Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) 
Research 
Laboratory of Medical Allergology, Dept. K, Allergy clinic 
SOP name: 
 
Gad c 1 ELISA 
Competitive Sandwich ELISA using Rabbit or FAST sera  
 
SOP no.: 
Version: 1 
Pages: 8 
Approved: 
Omfattet af akkreditering: 
JA ,  NEJ   
 
Content: 
Procedure for determination of parvalbumin (Gad c 1) content in cod extract and purified rCyp c 1 
Princip: 
 
1. Preparations of cod extracts from cod powders 
2. Coating with capture antibody (rabbit anti-Gad c 1) 
3. Blocking with EVB 
4. Incubation with cod extracts after preparation at different conditions 
5. Incubation with detection antibody (rabbit anti-Gad c 1-Biotin) 
6. Incubation with Avidin-peroxidase 
7. Color reaction with OPD 
8. ELISA reader, colorimetric measurement 
Supplement:  
• Gad c1 ELISA 
• Competitive Gad c1 ELISA with rabbit and human FAST sera 
Experimental timeframe: 2 days

SOP name:

p. 3   
 
This document is printed 14. august 2018 
 
Procedure: 
1. Preparations of cod extracts (day 1) 
 
Gad c 1 samples: 1 g Cod 1 (batch#1, cod 1.1) and Cod 2 is weight and transferred to a 15 ml 
centrifuge tube. 10 mL sterile water is added. 
The tubes are vortexed and placed in a rotor mixer (30 g/rmp (Intelli mixer RM-2M, program F1). 
The tubes are rotated in 1 hour at RT.  
The suspension was afterwards centrifuged at 2500x g/rmp, 10 min., RT, Accel/Deccel:8/8 (Rotina 
420R, Hettich) and the supernatant were pooled and transferred to new Eppendorf tubes for the 
second round of centrifugation at 18400xg, 10min., RT (Hermle Z 233M K, Ole Dich Aps). The 
supernatants from the tubes were pooled and aliquoted as 200/100 µl. The extracts were stored 
at - 20 °C  
 
Cod extracts were reproduced in larger amounts from Cod 1 powder and referred to as Cod 1 
batch# 2 (Cod 1.2). Cod 1.2 was quality ensured to be equal to Cod 1.1 by Gad c1 ELISA. 
 
2. Coating with capture antibody (rabbit anti-Gad c 1) 
Rabbit anti-Gad c 1 (2,5 mg/ml) is diluted to a concentration of 2 μg/ml (1:1250) in PBS  
10µl antibody + 12.5ml PBS 
100 μl pr. well is added with a multichannel pipette to a Maxisorp microtiter plate (ThermoFisher). 
Sealing tape is added to the plate. 
Incubation O/N at 4 °C (8-12°C degree). 
3. Blocking with EVB (Day 2) 
The plate is emptied for content and dried by slapping on paper. The plate is washed afterwards 
by:  
1. wash:  
200 μl EVB is added per. well and the plate is standing for 1 minute. 
 
The plate Is emptied and slapped dry. 
2. wash:  
200 μl EVB is added per. well and the plate is standing for 5 minutes. 
 
The plate Is emptied and slapped dry.  
200 μL EVB is added pr. well with a multichannel pipette. Sealing tape is added to the plate 
Incubation in 1 hour at RT.  
The plate is emptied for content and dried by slapping on paper. 
 
4. Incubation with cod extract at different conditions  
 
The cod extract is thawed up and centrifuged at 18400 g, 10 min, RT. 
Allergen dilutions are prepared and added to the plate, see supplement (page 5-8 ) for both 
Ordinary and competitive ELISA with rabbit and FAST sera 
 
5. Incubation with detection antibody (rabbit anti-Gad c 1-Biotin) 
 
The plate is emptied for content and slapped dried on paper. The plate is washed as follows:  
1. wash:  
200 μl EVB is added per. well and the plate is standing for 1 minute. 
 
The plate Is emptied and slapped dry. 
2. wash:  
200 μl EVB is added per. well and the plate is standing for 1 minutes. 
 
The plate Is emptied and slapped dry.  
==PAGE:121==
SOP name: 
SOP no.: 
p. 4   
 
This document is printed 14. august 2018 
 
3. wash:  
200 μl EVB is added per. well and the plate is standing for 5 minutes. 
 
The plate Is emptied and slapped dry.  
 
Rabbit anti-Gad c 1-Biotin (0,5mg/ml) is diluted to a concentration 5,4 μg/ml (1:110) in EVB. 
12.000µl EVB + 109µl antibody (12000:110=109) 
100 μl is added pr. well with a multichannel pipette. Sealing tape is added to the plate 
Incubation in 2 hours at 37°C. 
 
6. Incubation with Avidin-peroxidase 
The plate is emptied for content and slapped dried on paper. The plate is washed as follows:  
1. wash:  
200 μl EVB is added per. well and the plate is standing for 1 minute. 
 
The plate Is emptied and slapped dry. 
2. wash:  
200 μl EVB is added per. well and the plate is standing for 1 minutes. 
 
The plate Is emptied and slapped dry.  
3. wash:  
200 μl EVB is added per. well and the plate is standing for 5 minutes. 
 
The plate Is emptied and slapped dry.  
 
ExtrAvidin-Peroxidase is diluted 1:5000 in EVB. (3µl ExtrAvidin + 15mL EVB) 
100 μl is added pr. well with a multicanal pipette. Sealing tape is added to the plate 
Incubation in ½ hour at RT. 
 
 
7. Color reaction with OPD 
 
The plate is emptied for content and slapped dried on paper. The plate is washed as follows:  
1. wash:  
200 μl EVB is added per. well and the plate is standing for 1 minute. 
 
The plate Is emptied and slapped dry. 
2. wash:  
200 μl EVB is added per. well and the plate is standing for 1 minutes. 
 
The plate Is emptied and slapped dry.  
3. wash:  
200 μl EVB is added per. well and the plate is standing for 5 minutes. 
 
The plate Is emptied and slapped dry.  
 
2 OPD Tablets are dissolved in 18 mL sterile water and 2 mL Stable Peroxide Buffer is added. 
100 μl OPD-reagent is added pr. well with a multicanal pipette. 
The plate induces in 3-5 minutes (15-20 min.) in the dark (under an alum top).  
100 μL 0,5 M sulfuric acid is added pr. well, which stops the color reaction  
 
 
8. Reading 
The plate is read in : ELISA Reader (Absorbance Microplate Reader, Bio-Tek Instruments), using the 
program KC4 (Se SOP F80-1). The reading occurs at 490 nm (Ref 630 nm). 
 
Dangerous reagents 
OPD-tablets are carcinogenic and environmentally damaging. 
Brintoverilte/hydrogenperoxid 35% (conc.) is a health hazard 
 
Security equipment and procedure:  
Gloves are applied using OPD-tablets and when using hydrogenperoxid 35% (googles as well). 
Der anvendes handsker ved håndtering af OPD-tabletter.

Waste handling: 
 OPD-reagents rests as well as microtiter plates are thrown out in yellow waste buckets 
Other dilutions can be thrown out in the sink.

• 1:200  5µl + 995µl FB = 1000µl

Cod extracts 
Calculation for the content of Gad c1 in the extracts:  
Theory (R&D): 0.144g Gad c1/100 g fish = 0.00144g Gad c1 /g fish 
Extract: 1g cod powder/ 10ml H20 = 0.1g/ml 
(1g cod powder = 0.001440g Gad c1) = 0.00144g/10ml= 0.000144g Gad c1/ml = 0.144 mg Gad 
c1/mL = 144.000 ng/ml. 
 
To reach a start concentration of 144 ng/ml, Gad c 1 is diluted 1000 times: 
• 1:10   5µl Gad c1 + 45 µl FB = 50 µl  
• 1:100  5µl + 495µl FB = 500µl

Competitive sandwich ELISA using Rabbit serum or FAST serum  
 
Incubation with cod extract and rabbit or cod extract and FAST human (pre and post) IgG sera 
1 hour and O/N (18-20h) at 4 °C – all dilutions were prepared. Half was used after incubation (A+B) 
in 1 hour and the rest was kept for the next day.  
Extracts were collected from the freezer and centrifuged at 18400 g, 10 min, RT. 
 
The 500 µl contains: A (50%) + B (50%)   final conc. (1:100, 1:1000, 1:10000) 
A =  
• Constant for Rabbit sera (Cod 29 ng/mL) and FAST sera (cod 2.9 ng/ mL) 
B =  
• TAP5, TAP6, NKS   actual conc. (1:50, 1:500, 1:5000) 
• Post, Pre  actual conc. (1:50, 1:250, 1:500) 
• Buffer FB  
A+ B:  Competitive blocking samples  
• T5 + cod / T6 + cod / NKS + cod  final conc. (1:100, 1:1000, 1:10.000) 
• Pre-sera + cod  / Post-sera + cod    final conc. (1:100, 1:500, 1:1000) 
• FB + cod  14.5 ng/mL (rabbit model)  
• FB + cod  2.5 ng/mL (human model)

RABBIT MODEL : rabbit sera  
 
Cod volume (A): 
 (1g cod powder = 0.00144g Gad c1) = 0.144 mg Gad c1/mL = 144.000ng Gad c1/ml. 
To reach a final concentration at 29ng/mL, Gad c1 (Cod extract 1.2) was diluted 5000 times 
(144.000ng/ml / 5000 = 29 ng/mL):  
• 1:50  5µl + 245 µl FB = 250 µl 
• 1:100  30µl + 2970µl FB = 3000 µl (3mL)

• TAP5, 6, NKS 1:50  10µl rabbit + 490µl FB = 500 µl (rest 200µl) 
• TAP5, 6, NKS 1:500   50µl rabbit + 450 FB = 500 µl (rest 200µl) 
• TAP5, 6, NKS 1:5000   50µl rabbit + 450 FB = 500 µl (rest 200µl) 
• Buffer FB (250 …300 µl)

Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) 
Research 
  
Laboratory of Medical Allergology, Dept. K, Allergy clinic 
SOP name: 
Passive Sensitization of Basophils Using Buffy Coat 
Blood  
Competitive PS Basophil Model assay (Rabbit and 
Human models)  
 
Passiv sensibilisering af basofile fra buffy coat-blod. 
SOP no.: F68 - 2.1.0 
Version: 1 
Pages: 8 
Approved: 
Omfattet af akkreditering: 
JA ,  NEJ   
 
Content: 
 
1. Passive sensitization  
 
Stripping 
 
Passive sensitization and cell activation 
 
2. Preparation of competitive (blocking/inhibitory) samples (cod extract (and rCyp c 1)  + 
TAP5, TAP6 + NKS / FAST sera + We) 
 
3. Supplement  
Dilution examples 
HI-plate setup examples 
  
 
Principle: 
 
In this procedure, donor basophils suitable for passive sensitization are found beforehand in 
SOP: Buffy coat screening (Day 0). The passive sensitization (PS) procedure describes how to 
remove the autologous IgE from the basophils (stripping) and how to add new IgE (PS).  PS is 
performed simultaneously with competitive sera samples. PS basophil cell activation is 
performed by adding the stimulants of interest (allergen, anti-IgE, PMA/I) and released 
histamine is quantified.

Procedure: 
 
Initially, before running experiments with rabbit sera and FAST sera, a PS (pre-PS) is 
performed with 1362-57 and We pool (plate setup is similar to SOP : Buffy coat screening 
(Day 0). 
 
Sera and extracts are collected from the freezer and centrifuged at 18400 g, 10 min, RT. 
 
1. Passive sensitization 
This procedure removes the autologous IgE from the basophils (stripping) and replaces it with 
new IgE (passive sensitization). Both stripping volume and passive sensitization volume can be 
scaled up and down. 
 
Stripping  
Never use more than 5 mL buffy coat blood per 50 mL-tube due to reduced buffer capacity 
 
1. 
Invert blood before use. Use 5 mL buffy coat blood (4 plates) and 45 mL Sodium 
chloride 9 mg/mL.  16 full HI-plates: 20mL buffy coat + 180 mL NaCl  4 tubes of 5 
mL buffy coat + 45 NaCl 
 
2. 
Centrifuge; 1000 xg, Accel/Deccel: 5/3, 10 min. 11°C. Note red blood cells must pellet. 
This acceleration/deceleration values is low to avoid disturbing the cell layer. 
 
3. 
Remove supernatant down to 5 mL - avoid disturbing the white cell layer. 
 
 
Add cold (4°C) strip buffer up to 50 mL. 
 
4.        Centrifuge; 1000 xg, Accel/Deccel: 5/3, 15 min. 11 °C.  
 
 
Note red blood cells must pellet. 
 
==PAGE:129==
SOP name: 
 
SOP no.: 
p. 4   
 
 
 
This document is printed 14. august 2018 
 
5. 
Remove supernatant down to 5 mL - avoid disturbing the white cell layer. 
Add pipes buffer up to 50 mL. The stripping solution is removed fast due to low pH 
(bad for the basophils) and pipes is added to restore the pH condition. 
 
6.           Centrifuge; 1000 xg, Accel/Deccel: 5/3, 10 min. 11°C.  
 
 
Note red blood cells must pellet. 
 
7. 
Remove supernatant down to 5 mL (in all 4 tubes) and mix the cell suspension. 
 
 
 
Passive sensitization  
8. 
Centrifuge serum samples at 1840g, 10min at RT  
 
9. 
Use 125 µL serum + 1 mL cell suspension (Rabbit sera).  94 µL serum + 0,75 mL cell 
suspension (Pre-PS: 1362-57 + We, and FAST sera)  
 
10. 
Incubate: serum+ cell suspension and competitive samples (see 2. procedure) for 
minimum 60 min. at 37 °C. 
 
11. 
HI-Plate: 
Add 25 µL pipes buffer to standard (column 1)/blank-wells (row 1 and 2) on HI-plate 
and add desired samples (25 µL) :  Always dilutions with aIgE, allergen (cod extract 
and rCyp c 1), PMA/Ionomycin. (see different plate-setup in 3. Supplements)  
 
12. 
When cell suspension has incubated, add pipes buffer up to 3 mL ( or 2.25 mL ) and 
mix well. 
 
13. 
Add 25 µL serum + cell suspension to all wells on HI plates. 
 
14. 
Put a lid on the plates and incubate them for minimum 60 min. at 37 °C. 
 
15. 
The calibration plate is prepared, doing following: 
- 50µl pipes buffer 
- 30 min incubation at 37°C 
- Wash with demineralised water x5 times 
- 75µl OPA for 10 min.  
- 75µl pherchloric acid 0.59% to stop the colormetric development 
- Ready for HR reading/calibration 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:130==
SOP name: 
 
SOP no.: 
p. 5   
 
 
 
This document is printed 14. august 2018 
 
Quantification of released histamine 
 
3. 
Wash plates Wash plates 5x with demineralised water starting with column 1.  
Dry plates by slapping them repeatedly onto thick layers of absorbing paper.  (You can 
stop here and leave the plates up-side-down in the draw, until analysis). 
  
4. 
Add 150 μL SDS Solution 0,4% and incubate plates for 10 min at 37°C. 
 
5. 
Wash plates manually with demineralised water (5x2 both ways to make sure that the 
SDS is removed completely), dry plates.   
 
6. 
Add 75 μL OPA Solution to all wells – remember to start the timer at the first 
plate/first well. OPA react with the primary amines in histamine within the glass fibers 
 
7. 
After 10 min, stop the reaction by adding 75 µL perchloric acid 0,59 %.  
 
 
Allow the reaction to occur for a few minutes and read the plates on HistaReader.  
 
2. Preparation of competitive (blocking/inhibitory) samples (cod extract (and rCyp c 1)  + 
TAP5, TAP6 + NKS / FAST sera + We) 
Preparations (2) is performed simultaneously with PS stripping (1)  
 
 
Rabbit model:  
The 500 µl sample contains: A (50%, 250 µl) + B (50%, 250µl) 
A = cod extract constant (5.760ng/mL)  A+B  2.880 ng/mL 
B = sera   
• TAP5/ TAP6 / NKS  actual conc. (1:50, 1:500, 1:5000) 
A+ B:  
• TAP5 + cod / TAP6 + cod / NKS + cod   final conc. (1:100, 1:1000, 1:10.000) 
 
Human model: 
The 100 µl sample contains: A (50%, 70 µl) + B (50%, 70 µl) 
A = cod extract constant (2.880ng/mL)  A+B  1.440 ng/mL 
A = rCyp c 1 constant (10 ng/mL)  A+B  5 ng/mL  
B = sera  
• Pre-sera / Post-sera actual conc. (1:50, 1:250, 1:500) 
A+ B:  Competitive blocking samples  
• Pre-sera + cod / Post-sera + cod / We + cod  final conc. (1:100, 1:500, 1:1000)

3. Supplement: 
 
Cod extract dilution (A):  
100mg powder/mL = 100.000µg/ml. To reach a start concentration of 100µg/ml, a dilution to 
1:1000 (100.000/100µg/ml) is performed. 1:1000 dilution: 
• 1:10  50µl extract + 450 µl Pipes  
• 1:100  10µl + 990µl Pipes = 1000µl  
 
rCyp c 1 dilution (A):  
Cyp c1 concentration in tube: 1mg/mL = 1.000.000 ng/mL 
Desired start concentration: 100 ng/mL  
1.000.000 ng/mL
100𝑛𝑔/𝑚𝐿 
= 10.000 →  1: 10.000 𝑑𝑖𝑙𝑢𝑡𝑖𝑜𝑛 
1:10.000 fortynding: 
• 1:100  10µl + 990µl Pipes   
• 1:10  200µl rCyp + 1800 µl Pipes

Human model: Pre, Post  (sera, B): 
 
Pre and Post-sera :  
A volume of minimum 150 µl is needed per dilution: 
1. Pre,Post 1:50  5µl human + 245µl Pip = 250 µl  
2. Pre,Post 1:250   50µl human+ 200 Pip = 250 µl  
3. Pre,Post 1:500   50µl human + 450 Pip = 500 µl 
We plate (enough for all plates): 
1. 1:50  25µl + 1225µl Pip 
2. 1:250  250µl + 1000µl Pip 
3. 1:500  100µl + 900µl Pip 
 
70 µl Pre, Post + 70 µl Cod = 100 µl 
400µl We + 400 Cod, rCyp c 1  = 800 µl  
400µl pip + 400 Cod, rCyp c 1 = 800 µl
